Current Commentary

The So-Called Fundamental Principles of the Japanese 6

Since ancient times, the Japanese have seized rights in the Northeast using nothing but cunning conspiracies and nothing but seemingly gentle but inwardly vicious means. In the past, Chinese authorities were deceived by such conspiracies and tactics, and many unknowingly fell into their trap. Now, the Japanese are again attempting to use such conspiracies and tactics in the open arena where the powerful representatives of Geneva are gathered. The representatives of various countries will surely be amazed by the Japanese's sinister and treacherous intentions and become aware. What is meant by sinister and treacherous? It is the heavily veiled phrase "fundamental principles" in their counterproposal. Several days ago, Tokyo had already released the atmosphere of five demands, and there were also rumors in the Geneva discourse that were half believed and half doubted. We had long anticipated that the Japanese would use this tactic for probing. Until yesterday, when the representatives' counterproposal was presented, there was again talk of so-called fundamental principles that must first be negotiated with China before the troop withdrawal. However, the League of Nations had stated yesterday that it had heard absolutely nothing about these so-called fundamental principles. Today, in the open discussion of this issue, the chairman questioned the Japanese representative's intentions. The Japanese representative evasively replied that it was only to ensure the safety of the Japanese. When other representatives pressed him on whether it was only to ensure safety, he shifted the blame, saying that he only knew a little about their meaning and that the government had not yet permitted him to disclose it. When asked further, he avoided answering. That the Japanese representative wanted the League of Nations representatives to indicate their commitment to the fundamental principles without showing the representatives what the fundamental principles were, so that they could first understand the truth, was already extremely shocking. Moreover, when pressed, he still kept it a secret. It was either Yoshizawa intentionally playing the representatives in the palm of his hand, or the content must contain something not permitted by law and justice and could not be divulged to outsiders. The Japanese using such unscrupulous means to deal with the League of Nations was certainly unacceptable to the League of Nations, and deceiving the League of Nations with vague and confusing means was also something the League of Nations could not allow. We secretly hope that the League of Nations will adhere to its just claims and not allow the sinister and treacherous Japanese to succeed in their plot.

Although the Japanese's sinister and treacherous means seem extremely mysterious and undisclosed, in the eyes of the world, it must be nothing more than the five demands released earlier. But in addition to these five demands, how can we know that they will not make other excuses to achieve their goals? Therefore, our entire nation should pay particular attention to these so-called fundamental principles. Whether they are outside the five demands or within the five demands, we should unite with a spirit of swearing to die to break their sinister and treacherous means.

Before this reporter finished drafting, he received the latest news. The League of Nations resolution has been passed by a vote in the assembly. The Japanese counterproposal has also been unanimously rejected. The League of Nations has been able to uphold its justice and has not been swayed by the power of the strong. How will our people work harder, unite with the League of Nations, and resist this powerful power of conspiracy and trickery?

Receiving Important Domestic Telegrams 7

Regarding any restrictions on industrial organizations, in short, the original situation before the incident should be fully restored. The current request is for the League of Nations Administrative Council and the U.S. representative to indicate their acceptance of the invitation to be sent by the Chinese government, and to appoint representatives to jointly implement the fourth item of the resolution with the Chinese government. The Chinese government considers the following points to be the most important: that the withdrawal of troops in the sixth item of the resolution is the most important issue for the Administrative Council at present. Other matters will not be discussed until the troop withdrawal is completed. However, another point that must be clarified is that the Chinese government believes that in addition to the troop withdrawal issue, there are also issues of responsibility and the estimated losses of the Chinese side after September 18th. From the beginning, the Chinese government has been willing to hand this matter over to a neutral third country for decision in accordance with the principles of the League of Nations. However, using the occupation of Manchuria as an opportunity to forcibly resolve other demands is contrary to the spirit of the Covenant and violates Article 2 of the Pact of Paris. Under the oppression of armed occupation, or under conditions created by force, China will never negotiate any issues with any country. This point is the foundation for the establishment of the League of Nations and the Pact of Paris. The Chinese government believes that this is a fundamental issue and therefore makes this special solemn declaration. The Chinese government is confident that by adhering to this attitude, it will receive unconditional moral assistance from all members of the League of Nations and all parties to the Pact of Paris. Any negotiations between China and any country on any issue must be conducted based on China's inherent rights and obligations under the Covenant and the Pact of Paris, and must respect the principles governing the relationship between China and other countries as stipulated in the Washington Conference. Regarding this matter, I would like to

Page 8

make an extremely clear and solemn declaration. Once this unfortunate incident is resolved and normal relations are restored, it will be known that the Chinese government is not only willing but also eagerly hopes to negotiate all issues between China and Japan in a spirit of great friendship. China's only wish is to live in peace with all countries, especially to be on friendly terms with its neighbors. It is also hoped that although the two countries have been greatly agitated and appealed to the League of Nations this time, this agitation may lead both sides to resolutely seek an improvement in the relationship between the two countries in the future and seek to build a foundation for permanent peace in the Far East. In this spirit, the Chinese government welcomes the Administrative Council's proposal to establish a permanent reconciliation committee or similar mechanism. Furthermore, I can assure the League of Nations that the Chinese government will not only carefully abide by all obligations within the public law of the League of Nations to promote good neighborly relations with Japan, but will also strive to shift the thinking of its people towards peace and friendship in order to forget the painful past and hope for a better future. (24th Special Telegram)

The Executive Yuan Discussed the So-Called Basic Principles Yesterday Morning 8

British Representative Demands a Clear Explanation

Yoshizawa Indicates It Is Difficult to Officially Announce

(Geneva) The Council reconvened this morning. After debating the value of the Council's resolution and Japan's counter-proposal, Yoshizawa, the chief Japanese representative, announced that he could not accept the Council's draft resolution for resolving the Sino-Japanese Manchurian dispute. The Council was struck by this declaration like a bolt from the blue and immediately announced a postponement until 4 p.m. No vote was taken on either the Council's resolution or Japan's counter-proposal. When the situation became tense before the postponement, the Spanish representative, Madariaga, made a final effort to reach an agreement and proposed an amendment stipulating that direct diplomatic negotiations should begin between the two sides on the day the Japanese troops completed their withdrawal, in order to resolve their disputes. The term "basic principles" is now a real obstacle to resolving the dispute between China and Japan. Japan refused to explain these four words to the Council. The Council refused to accept Japan's counter-proposal until the Japanese representative had thoroughly explained the meaning of the four words "basic principles" as mentioned by the Tokyo government. The final efforts of this afternoon's meeting are generally seen as hopeless. Yoshizawa replied to the Spanish representative's amendment, saying that Japan could not allow the detailed explanation of the four words "basic principles" in the Council, and could not allow anyone other than China to discuss these four words. Japan cannot withdraw the four words "basic principles" from its counter-proposal. Briand then replied that the Council could not include these four words in the resolution without first knowing the Japanese intent. At this point, Yoshizawa rose and said, "I must reiterate that Japan has no intention of resolving the Manchurian issue by force." (24th National Telegram)

(Geneva) After the League of Nations Administrative Council met this morning, it focused on the issue of the so-called basic principles. In its counter-proposal, Japan requested that the Chinese and Japanese governments have an agreement on the basic principles governing ordinary relations before the withdrawal of troops from Manchuria. What exactly does Japan mean by this request? Is it solely focused on guaranteeing its own safety against retaliation, or does it intend to include events between the two countries that have differed for a long time in the basic principles? The British representative, Cecil, asked the Japanese representative to clearly explain the meaning of this phrase. Yoshizawa replied that he knew the meaning of the basic principles to some extent, but he could not speak for the Administrative Council until the Japanese government allowed him to announce it. He believed that it was only natural for the Japanese government to conclude an agreement with China before the withdrawal of troops. The Japanese government is well aware that if this is not the case, Japanese people will be in danger of being retaliated against by the Chinese. Finally, he said that he had given a sufficient explanation of the basic principles. Briand then announced an adjournment until 4 p.m., at which time a vote would be taken to decide on the Administrative Council's draft resolution and Japan's counter-proposal. (24th Reuters Telegram)

(Geneva) Today's meeting began a few minutes after 10 a.m. Although it was raining heavily, there were still many observers. President Briand spoke first, saying that the purpose of this meeting was to continue the discussion of the Administrative Council's draft and Japan's counter-proposal.

Yoshizawa then made a very important announcement, saying that the basic principles mentioned in Japan's counter-proposal were intended to protect the safety of the Japanese people, and that other events that the two countries had been unable to agree on for a long time could be discussed later. Thus, the issue of basic principles was included in what Briand called the first category of events yesterday.

The Spanish representative, Madariaga, asked in clear and reasonable terms whether the basic principles were only related to the safety of Japanese lives after the withdrawal of Japanese troops, and said that he regretted that the Japanese representative's explanation could not satisfy him. For the sake of Japan's interests, the Japanese representative should explain these principles in detail to avoid future doubts. What he worried about was that the Japanese government not only wanted to ease the situation, but also wanted to discuss other outstanding issues in order to ease the situation. The Spanish representative also said that there was an easy solution to this problem. After the Japanese troops withdrew, they should be allowed to decide on direct negotiations, which should begin on the day of the withdrawal. The length of the withdrawal period could be arranged.

Cecil also joined the debate, saying that the Japanese representative had asked him to pay attention to the news in the newspapers about the basic things that Japan wanted, that is, the news about discussing the treaty issue between China and Japan. He wanted to know that we are not responsible for the news in the newspapers, but I would like to ask you to pay attention to a matter that can be studied greatly. I would like to read a telegram sent from Tokyo to London by the Reuters representative. The text said that Japanese officials believe that if the League of Nations refuses to deal with the issue of the sanctity of treaties, it should not try to force Japan to change its position, etc. Cecil also said that the Administrative Council had not heard of any intention to raise the issue of treaties, but we now know from a world-famous news agency that Japanese officials have announced that Japan cannot change its position. I think Yoshizawa can admit that a serious misunderstanding may occur. Since the League of Nations Charter stipulates the respect for various treaty obligations, the issue of the sanctity of treaties has not arisen. The effectiveness of the interpretation of the provisions may be disputed, but this dispute can be resolved by the Hague Court. The current chairman of the court is a Japanese. Cecil also said that he did not see any difficulty for Japan in expressing its opinions, but this is completely different from the announcement of discussions before the withdrawal of troops. In his opinion, the presidential procedure is definitely the opposite of the order of events.

Yoshizawa replied to Madariaga and Cecil's remarks, saying that the Japanese government was prepared to withdraw its troops as soon as it was sure of the safety of its people and property. As for the issue of the sanctity of treaties, there must be a misunderstanding. He had not telegraphed this opinion to the government. The Reuters news was very regrettable. He would now telegraph this matter to the government. President Briand ended the debate, saying that the original text of the Administrative Council's draft was moved by the idea of respecting treaties, but there should be no long-term negotiations before the withdrawal of troops. The fundamental difference between the two sides lies in what should be done to protect the safety of the Japanese people. The Japanese representative has provided many explanations, but what he explained still shows some vague remarks about basic principles. Yoshizawa is one of the most ardent supporters of the League of Nations, so he is not a person who conceals himself by being vague, but in fact, there is indeed vagueness. Briand also announced to Yoshizawa that when the discussion of the Administrative Council had not yet been infected with political bacteria, the Japanese government had undertaken to carry out the withdrawal of troops that had already begun as soon as possible on the condition that the safety of the Japanese people was fully guaranteed. This declaration already contained the recognition that the safety of the Japanese people could be guaranteed. The resolution of this issue is a matter of the dignity of the League of Nations.

Briand went on to mention Article 10 of the League of Nations Charter and Article 11 of the Paris Convention, saying that these articles are very clear. He thought that Japan knew its obligations well, but public opinion could not accept military occupation before direct negotiations. Briand also mentioned the news read in the Administrative Council's repeated meetings, saying that he did not want to introduce external debates and news. He was afraid that the Japanese government intended to introduce outstanding issues into the discussion, but Yoshizawa had declared to the Administrative Council that these issues would only be discussed after the withdrawal of troops. Japan's eagerness for the safety of its people is very natural, but he knew that if there was no military pressure, the situation could return to normal. The League of Nations has already made a great contribution to humanity in this regard.

Briand then proposed that Japan's counter-proposal should be discussed. If it was rejected, then unless China and Japan proposed another method, the Administrative Council's proposal should be considered.

Madariaga said that the basic principles that had been discussed had not been defined. He felt that it was difficult to find a country today that had a greater sense of honor than Japan, but he was very disappointed with Japan's attitude.

Then Yoshizawa explained in very unclear terms, saying that the Japanese government believed that the basic principles should not be raised on the seats of the Administrative Council, but should only be discussed by both sides. It is absolutely necessary to negotiate and list an agreement containing these principles in advance. Therefore, I cannot withdraw the basic principle numbers in the counter-proposal, and I cannot accept the Administrative Council's resolution without guaranteeing the safety of Japanese residents. Japan does not want to resolve the Manchurian case by force.

Madariaga proposed that Japan should withdraw its counter-proposal and the Administrative Council's resolution should be amended to give Japan a more certain security guarantee in the form of a solemn declaration to the Administrative Council by both parties. Briand then turned to Yoshizawa and said in a most sincere tone that no words with unclear meanings could be inserted into the resolution. The Administrative Council then announced a postponement until 5 p.m. Today's meeting has aroused great anger here. The general public is also frightened by the prolonged stalemate. (24th Reuters Telegram)

Japan Resents Britain 9

Japanese Cabinet Held a Special Meeting Yesterday

(Tokyo) Japan is now quite resentful of Britain because of the Manchurian case. It is reported that the League of Nations' strong attitude towards Japan is partly due to the British Ambassador to China, Lampson, and the British Foreign Secretary, Reading. The Asahi Shimbun and other newspapers carried news of the talks between the British and Japanese ambassadors in Ningxia on October 17, saying that Lampson had instructions to advise Japan to withdraw from the occupied areas before negotiations. Lampson also said that the Japanese military authorities should allow Zhang Xueliang to return to Shenyang. Although officials here have not spoken about this news, they are quite angry. Many Japanese newspapers have published editorials criticizing Britain's anti-Japanese conspiracy, saying that Britain wants to befriend China in order to restore its lost position, so it forced the League of Nations to invite the United States to participate in the Geneva Conference in order to put pressure on Japan. Britain actually abandoned its old friendship with Japan and stood on the side of China, focusing its strength to force Japan to withdraw its troops. It should be known that Britain itself is now stationing troops in Shanghai to protect the lives and property of British people. It is unforgivable that it does not understand Japan's position. (24th Reuters Telegram)

(Tokyo) The cabinet held a special meeting this morning to consider the League of Nations' proposals on the Manchurian case, such as the Japanese military withdrawing by November 16. (24th Reuters Telegram)

(Tokyo) Japanese officials seem to believe that if the League of Nations refuses to deal with the issue of the sanctity of treaties, it should not try to force Japan to change its position. Japan must insist on the binding of China's recognition of the treaty as an indispensable condition, but the League of Nations does not care about it. Officials are disappointed and regretful. There is also talk of considering withdrawing from the League of Nations. It is heard that the reason why the Secretary-General of the League of Nations, Drummond, decided not to submit the first plan that Japan could accept to the Administrative Council was because after final consideration, he felt that it was impossible to make China agree to recognize all the binding conditions. Therefore, he decided to put forward the third plan. At the same time, the Secretary-General informally suggested to Yoshizawa that Japan could ask the Hague Court to handle this issue, but the Japanese believed that if the League of Nations was unwilling to deal with fundamental issues such as the sanctity of treaties, then the entire foundation of the League of Nations would be shaken. (24th Reuters Telegram)

The Special Foreign Affairs Committee Resolved to Accept the Draft Resolution of the League of Nations 10

(Nanjing) The Special Foreign Affairs Committee held a meeting at the Central Party Headquarters at 11 a.m. on the 24th to discuss the draft resolution of the League of Nations. As a result, it was decided to accept it and further promote the League of Nations to force Japan to fulfill its obligations on schedule, so that the Japanese would no longer have any objections. (24th Special Telegram)

(Nanjing) Regarding the draft resolution of the League of Nations Council on the Sino-Japanese issue, the government telegraphed Shi Zhaoji on the 23rd, instructing him to express acceptance in order to show that our country has always respected the public opinion of the League of Nations. When the Special Foreign Affairs Committee held a meeting on the 24th, it raised this case for discussion and decided to telegraph Shi again, instructing the League of Nations to adhere to the original resolution of the draft without making any concessions. (24th Special Telegram)

The Issue of Treaty Binding 11

The Main Reason for Japan's Insistence

(Tokyo) According to reliable sources, the former Chinese Foreign Minister Wang insisted during the Sino-Japanese negotiations on consular jurisdiction that Japan must return the South Manchurian Railway and the Liaodong Leased Territory, including Lushun and Dalian, to China before China could agree that the Japanese had the right to live in the interior of China. Japan was therefore panicked. This is one of the main reasons for insisting that China should recognize the binding of various treaties. (24th Reuters Telegram) (Tokyo) The Japanese government, because Yoshizawa obviously misunderstood the previous instructions, has instructed Yoshizawa to explain to the League of Nations Administrative Council that Japan included the 1915 treaty (referring to the Twenty-One Demands) in the "existing treaty binding" that China must recognize. It also ordered Yoshizawa to ask the Administrative Council

Page 9

Receiving Important Domestic Telegrams II 12

to record the five key points of Japan. When Cecil raised questions about the meaning of the basic points stated in Japan's statement at the Administrative Council meeting, Yoshizawa did not list them one by one. The Secretary-General of the League of Nations, Drummond, seemed to have told Yoshizawa that he was hesitant not to ask China to recognize the 1915 treaty because if the demand for recognition was a prerequisite, the resolution of the troop withdrawal issue would be prolonged. Drummond also suggested to Yoshizawa that Japan should be satisfied with China's recognition of the treaty of mutual recognition, so that it could abandon the 1915 treaty, which China insisted was signed under oppression and had never recognized. However, the Japanese representative stood firm, saying that other powers had recognized the validity of the 1915 treaty, so the abolition of this article was not a problem. According to Japan's view, the sanctity of treaties and the guarantee of peace are both the foundation of the League of Nations' existence. Therefore, if the League of Nations follows China's request based on the latter principle, the League of Nations should also accept Japan's request based on the former principle. (24th Reuters Telegram)

(Paris) The situation in which China accepted the Administrative Yuan's resolution without reservation, while Japan insisted on its original attitude and put forward a genuine counter-proposal, has been given considerable attention by the press. Shi's remarks and his political views have been implicitly revealed in the praises of various newspapers when reporting on the meeting. Yoshizawa's failure to answer Sir Cecil's accurate and tight questions has also been noted by various newspapers. General opinion Briand's restrictive interpretation of Japan's so-called basic principles in the resolution that Yoshizawa will eventually agree that at least a part of Japan's counter-proposal will be incorporated into yesterday's resolution does not seem impossible. If so, it would not be difficult to reach a final agreement at the final meeting held this morning. (24th Havas Agency Telegram)

The People of Heilongjiang Province Are Reassured 14

Restoration of the Jiangqiao Bridge on the Tao'ang Road

(Beiping) Harbin Telegram: (1) After Ma Zhanshan took over as acting chairman, he announced that Pu Bingshan was the commander of the Longjiang Garrison, and designated the First Artillery Regiment, the Second Infantry Regiment, and the First Cavalry Detachment as the garrison troops. Rumors gradually subsided and people's hearts were stabilized. (2) The Jiangqiao Bridge on the Tao'ang Road has been restored. The Tao'ang train traveled from Shiba Lidian Station to Maoxing Station on the 23rd. Along the way, there were 12 regiments of Heilongjiang troops, including artillery, cavalry, and infantry, and two regiments of Tunkun troops stationed, with solid defenses. The two brigades of Xu's troops under Zhang HaiPeng's command have gone to the Xing'an area for reorganization. (3) Japanese troops send four or five aircraft to reconnaissance in the Heihe and Nenjiang Bridge area every day. Anti-aircraft guns have been installed in the provincial capital for air defense. (24th Special Telegram)

(Beiping) Harbin Telegram: After Ma Zhanshan took over as acting chairman of Heilongjiang, he is now reorganizing the army. The public security in the provincial capital is maintained by Commander Liang of the Garrison. All students of the Military Academy are responsible for maintaining it. (24th Special Telegram)

(Beiping) This place received a telegram from the Heilongjiang authorities stating: (1) The Japanese troops in Taonan withdrew on the 16th, but to our surprise, a hundred more returned on the 22nd, acting suspiciously. The Nenjiang Railway Bridge was slightly damaged some time ago due to the invasion of Tao and Zhang, preventing their advance north. We should regard this move as a considerable military action. However, yesterday we received a note from the Japanese consulate, using the excuse that the Tao'ang Road was built with Japanese capital and intends to send workers from the South Manchurian Railway Company to repair it. Upon investigation, this action by the Japanese side is clearly using the excuse of repairing the bridge to cover up Tao and Zhang's invasion north, and it is even more inappropriate for the South Manchurian Railway Company, which is irrelevant, to send workers to build and repair the Tao'ang Road. In addition to having replied that the Nenjiang Railway Bridge should be repaired by our side, we also ask that this be widely disseminated internationally to clarify the truth. (24th Special Telegram)

Zhang HaiPeng Flees to Shenyang

His Troops Are Ordered to Be Reorganized by His Son

(Beiping) After Zhang HaiPeng's troops fled to Taonan, Zou Zuohua's Tunkun Army Regiment took over the defense of Tailai Town and continued to pursue. Japanese aircraft from time to time flew over Heilongjiang for reconnaissance. Qiqihar has installed anti-aircraft guns for defense. All the areas within the Jilin Railway Line are occupied by the Japanese army, and the rest are still in our hands. There are still seven or eight brigades of troops stationed there. Xi Qia personally does not have much strength. Huang Xiansheng, a representative of Zhang, has now gone to Heilongjiang to try to take in Zhang HaiPeng's troops. (24th Special Telegram)

(Harbin) After Zhang HaiPeng's army was defeated, it could not stand in Taonan. His troops were ordered to be reorganized by his son. On the 23rd, he fled from the Siping-Taonan Railway to Shenyang. Zhang HaiPeng's son, Zhi Ming, telegraphed to Ma Zhanshan, the chairman of Heilongjiang, asking him to stop military operations and not allow the Heilongjiang army to exert pressure again. On the 22nd, he also sent two representatives to Heihe to beg for mercy. Ma agreed that if Zhang's army did not invade, the Heilongjiang army would never advance. (24th Special Telegram)

(Harbin) Ma Zhanshan is offering a reward of 20,000 yuan for the arrest of Zhang HaiPeng. Two thousand unarmed Jilin soldiers who were disarmed arrived in Harbin yesterday, all without food and clothing. (24th Special Telegram)

Landmines Are Planted Along the Railway Line

If there was any doubt, the items would be detained. Those who did not have a transit pass were not allowed to enter Shenyang. (2) In Xinmin, Juliuhe, Huanggu Tun, and other places, the Japanese army was ordered to assemble troops and reorganize military equipment because General Shirakawa had just arrived in the Xinmin area for inspection. Before Shirakawa arrived, he decided to remove all obstacles in the vicinity. (3) The Japanese army has increased its forces at each station east of Xinmin on the 24th. Guard posts have been added to each bridge and branch road, forcing nearby farmers to investigate banditry. If they know the truth and hide it, they will be held jointly liable. The Japanese army also built barracks and set up tents, with no signs of withdrawal. The Japanese army conducted extremely strict searches between Juliuhe and Huanggu Tun, and no one was spared. U.S. Military Officer Refuses Japanese Army Inspection 18

The two sides argued for two hours, and the inspection was not carried out in the end. As a result, train No. 104 arrived in Tianjin at 4 a.m. on the 24th, delayed for two hours. Xi Qia Declares Reduction of Jilin Province Military Expenses 21

For Japan or for Jilin?

Japanese Military in Jilin Rampant with Lewd Authority 23

(Beiping) A person from Jilin reported that the majority of the Japanese troops in Jilin have retreated to Lianhua Pao in the east of the city. At 6 p.m., they all mobilized, creating a very tense situation. Each street and alley in the city is heavily guarded. If pedestrians are unaware, they often face death. Starting from the 11th, the Japanese military conducted heavy artillery exercises at Dongda Tan. Pedestrians were prohibited from 6 to 9 p.m. Those who entered or exited were forced to kneel on the side of the road for three hours. Hundreds were forced to kneel, a shameful sight. Japanese soldiers and merchants took photos and sold them. All bookstores and schools are strictly inspected. All anti-Japanese books are taken away. Inns in the third and fourth districts are searched. Several people have been killed. The searches are all conducted at 3 or 4 a.m., without allowing people to put on clothes. They are made to kneel naked in the courtyard. Any delay results in either death or beating. Any money found is immediately confiscated. Shops are forced to open their doors. Financial flow is disrupted. Newspapers from both domestic and international ports are prohibited from distribution. Recently, because the American investigation team is about to arrive, the Japanese suddenly forced the police stations to hang the Blue Sky White Sun flag to deceive Westerners. Prince Jin Xuzong of the Su Prince's Mansion has joined Japanese nationality and will become the Director of the Jichang and Jidun Railway Bureau on the 13th. He is subject to the orders of both Zhang Xi regarding military and political affairs in Ying County, taking a wait-and-see approach. The expenses of the Jilin Official Office are solely reliant on the income from Jilin and Changchun. Jilin University issued a notice to students that the start of the semester is indefinite. (24th Dispatch)

Anti-Japanese Association in Beijing Warns Japanese Government 30

(Nanjing) The Anti-Japanese Association of all circles in the capital telegraphed the Japanese government on the 24th, stating that according to reports, your government has actually telegraphed our government to stop the anti-Japanese movement of the people, which is absurd and shocking to the world. This anti-Japanese movement of our people is purely provoked by your country's aggression and cannot be instigated by anyone, nor can it be stopped by our government. It must be understood that the greater the pressure, the greater the resistance. The people of our country are full of boiling blood and are sworn enemies with your country's policy of aggression. If a bad outcome occurs, it will be greatly detrimental to your country. Therefore, we issue this early and serious warning, hoping that you will awaken as soon as possible. (24th Dispatch)

Japanese Merchants in Chinese Markets Will Suffer a Major Setback 31

(Nanjing) Among Japanese goods imported into China, the three northeastern provinces rank first, Shanghai ranks second, Tianjin ranks third, and Hankou ranks fourth. The annual sales of Japanese goods in Guangdong, Fujian, Xiamen, Qingdao, Taizhou, and other places also amount to several million to tens of millions. The majority of Japanese industry and commerce depend on Chinese money for expansion, and the country's economy largely depends on the prosperity of industry and commerce for maintenance. If China continues to boycott Japanese goods for more than a year, even if Japan is fierce, it will have no bullets to use against us. This is the consensus of those who understand the economic situation of Japan. According to a recent customs investigation, in the two weeks from the 18th of last month to the beginning of this month, imports to Shanghai decreased by two-thirds compared to the previous month, and the same is true for other ports. In the South China area, goods from the United States and Britain are actively operating in the market. Because Japanese goods are being boycotted, importers have turned to the United Kingdom, the United States, Germany, and other countries to order substitutes. According to international business observations, the Japanese have already fallen into extreme failure, and the development of the Chinese market will be led by the United Kingdom in the first place and the United States in the second. (24th Dispatch)

Central Government Urges Guangdong Representatives to Come to Beijing by Telegram 34

Important Foreign Telegrams

US-France Conference Begins 61

Seeking to Promote the Recovery of the World Economy

French Newspapers Express Doubt and Fear About German-Russian Cooperation

Washington, 23rd (KMT) The widely anticipated U.S.-France conference was held at the White House this evening. The main figures are U.S. President Hoover and French Prime Minister Laval. The matters discussed at this conference have not yet been announced. At the beginning of the meeting, in addition to Hoover and Laval, there were U.S. Deputy Secretary of the Treasury Mills and French economic expert Pichon. Later, Senator Borah, chairman of the Senate Foreign Relations Committee, joined temporarily. Borah told people afterwards that he had a very deep impression of Laval after the meeting, and Laval praised Borah and wanted to have a deeper discussion again, so it has now been decided that Laval and Borah will meet at Stimson's private residence on Saturday afternoon. In short, Borah's temporary invitation to the White House to participate in the U.S.-France conference has attracted outside attention. The U.S.-France meeting this evening lasted for several hours, but the content of the talks is rarely known to the outside world. Later, Laval actually stayed at the White House, sleeping in the walnut bed that Lincoln used to sleep in.

Washington, 24th (Reuters) Regarding the official statement on French Prime Minister Laval's visit to the United States, it has now been issued, stating that the French Prime Minister's talks with President Hoover only concerned the policies that the two governments could develop to promote the recovery of the world economy.

Washington, 24th (Reuters) French journalists who reported on French Prime Minister Laval's actions in the United States met with Senator Borah. Borah stated that the revision of the Treaty of Versailles is an imminent matter. It is now becoming increasingly clear that this treaty will eventually be revised by peaceful or forceful means. If the Allied countries cancel Germany's reparations, he can agree to cancel the Allied countries' war debts to the United States. He hopes that France will decide its own degree of disarmament, but if certain situations arising from the Treaty of Versailles continue to exist, he does not see the possibility of European disarmament.

Paris, 23rd (KMT) French public opinion is now focused on the U.S.-France conference. A reporter from the Paris Victory Newspaper stated that there is now an extremely anti-Soviet expression in American political circles. Washington's general politicians and officials are quite uneasy about the progress of the Soviet Union's five-year construction plan. The newspaper also stated that European countries are now accepting warnings and must quickly sever all existing relations with the Soviet Union before the issue of war debt and reparation reduction can be hoped to be approved by the U.S. Congress, that is, the prospect of extending President Hoover's debt repayment plan also depends on this move. In addition to the Victory Newspaper, other newspapers also reported that the Russian issue will occupy a very important position in the current U.S.-France talks. The Paris Morning Post stated that Germany is seeking economic assistance from France on the one hand, and on the other hand, it allows the Soviet Union to purchase goods on credit in Germany, with Germany's national guarantee. The United States is extremely dissatisfied with this matter. It is heard that President Hoover, Secretary of State Stimson, and Secretary of the Treasury Mellon have all unanimously expressed that if Germany cannot sever all relations with the Soviet Union, the United States strongly disapproves of German-French cooperation, because the Soviet Union's purchase of all kinds of machinery and supplies in Germany on credit is to promote the five-year construction plan and cause a great harm to the world's industry and commerce.

London Silver Price Contracts by 125 62

London, 24th (KMT) Today's London silver market closing price, both near and far terms contracted by 125. The near term is 17 pence 1875, and the far term is 17 pence 25, while yesterday the near term was 17 pence 3125 and the far term was 17 pence 375.

News

Another Car Robbery on the Beining Railway 63

Bandits Well-Equipped and Organized

Passengers Fortunately Uninjured, Losses Huge

Tianjin Correspondence: The section of the Beining Railway outside the customs has been open to traffic for nearly a month. In the past month, it has been bombed by Japanese planes and strafed by machine guns, and plundered by bandits no less than a dozen times. The magnitude of the losses and the depth of the suffering are unspeakable. This is all due to the Japanese army's violent occupation of Liaoning and Jilin and their collaboration with bandits, resulting in the devastation of the local area and creating an atmosphere of unease. Today (the 22nd) at 0:59 AM, the 106th train on the Beining Railway was completely robbed when it arrived at Baimiaozi Station. I inquired with the Railway Bureau and obtained the following details: About 20 minutes before the robbery, about 400 to 500 bandits, armed with submachine guns and rifles, rushed into the stationmaster's office at Baimiaozi Station. They first cut the long-distance telephone and telegraph lines, and then tried to smash the track signal bell. After Stationmaster Dong's repeated negotiations, the track signal was not destroyed. The bandits then monitored the stationmaster and workers and began to rob. More than 300 yuan of the station's funds and the stationmaster's private funds were robbed, and the stationmaster's clothes were also stolen. The homes of other employees and workers were also robbed. The bandits then went to the police station at the station to rob and pointed their guns at the stationmaster, forcing him to open the door. The police station had no choice but to hand over their weapons. The bandits knew that the 106th train would depart from Xingcheng at 0:40 AM and arrive at Baimiaozi Station. They forced the workers from the engineering department to remove a section of the track at the west entrance of the station and remove the red light sign. At 0:59 AM, when the train arrived at the entrance of Baimiaozi Station, locomotive No. 313 derailed at the damaged track. The bandits opened fire on the train, and the guards returned fire. However, they were outnumbered, and their weapons were confiscated. Then, the bandits rushed onto the train, drove the passengers off, and robbed all the passengers' luggage, clothes, and the luggage in the luggage car, leaving nothing untouched. This lasted for more than an hour and a half. At about 2:00 AM, the bandits gathered at the station, called roll, and fled to the northwest. The bandits were well-equipped and organized, and it seemed that there were Japanese and Korean ruffians among them. After the incident, the station urgently telegraphed Zhang Jianxu's troops of the 12th Brigade for assistance. They did not arrive until dawn, and the bandits had long fled. It is said that no passengers were injured, but the train conductor, Cai Qingliang, was injured in the waist, and the car guard, Wei Yinzhong, also suffered minor injuries. The exact amount of the loss is still under investigation. (22nd)

Hunan Veterans Organize National Salvation Volunteer Army 64

Changsha Correspondence: Since the Northeast Incident occurred, the people of Hunan Province have been extremely indignant and have established (1) the Hunan Students' Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association, (2) the Hunan People from All Walks of Life's Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association, and (3) the Hunan Youth Iron-Blood National Salvation Corps to carry out national salvation work. Hunan Province has always been the place where the most soldiers are produced. No matter what war in the country, there are Hunan soldiers participating. In the past downsizing and demobilization, there are as many as one or two million veterans in Hunan Province. Now, Luo Xiankai and others have initiated the organization of the Hunan Veterans National Salvation Volunteer Army, gathering veterans to act as a diplomatic backing. At one time, more than 1,000 people, including Chen Binsheng, Wang Bangji, Cao Chucai, Peng Guanhe, Zhang Shuxun, Tao Caiju, Liang Quan, and He Xiang, joined upon hearing the news. A preparatory office has been temporarily set up at the Tongan Hostel in Xipailou to actively carry out the work. The reasons for the organization and the brief regulations have been submitted to the relevant authorities for record. The brief regulations are recorded as follows: (Article 1) Veterans voluntarily unite to save the country, unite as one, assist the government, and jointly deal with Japan. The details are as follows: A. Support the government and obey orders. B. Accept the guidance of the party and believe in the Three Principles of the People. C. Implement military training. D. Take the Premier's love and sincerity as the foundation for uniting comrades. (Article 2) Determination of name and implementation steps: A. The name is determined as the Hunan Veterans National Salvation Volunteer Army. B. A preparatory office is temporarily set up and cadres are established to promote implementation. C. The preparatory office is temporarily located at Tongan Hostel in Xipailou. D. The preparatory office has a number of committee members, with seven standing committee members elected. The committee is divided into five sections: Secretary, General Affairs, Public Relations, Publicity, and Organization, with one director and several staff members in each section. After the organization is complete, the headquarters will be officially established. E. When necessary, branch offices may be established in various counties to expand the organization. (Article 3) Regulations that members of this team should abide by are divided into the following points: A. All veterans who are willing to join must be introduced by two team members and fill in a letter of intent for review, registration, and awaiting formation and training. B. All members of this team must obey orders, strictly abide by discipline, cultivate a spirit of mutual assistance, and be a model for soldiers. C. If any member of this team goes beyond the scope or does not abide by the regulations, military punishment will be implemented. (Article 4) Qualifications of team members are divided into the following points: A. Age from 25 to 50 years old. B. Those who have received military training. C. Those who have no addictions. D. Those who are physically strong and have no diseases or disabilities. E. Those who have no suspicions of being bandits or communists. F. Those who have been deprived of their civil rights and have not been restored cannot join. (Article 5) Military uniforms, salaries, equipment, and supplies are divided into the following points: A. Freely donated by the people. B. Military uniforms will not be unified for the time being. They will be reissued when the economy is active. C. Supplies will be paid from the donated funds. D. Service officers and soldiers will not be paid for the time being. E. Formal expenses will be made for those who are sent out on official business, and actual expenses will be reported and reimbursed. (Article 6) The organization of the headquarters is divided into the following points: A. The headquarters has three brigades, the brigades have three detachments, the detachments have three battalions, the battalions have three companies, and the companies have three squads. Each squad has three classes, with eleven people in each class. B. The headquarters is divided into seven sections: General Affairs, Documents, Personnel, Public Relations, Management, Education, and Publicity. The directors are elected by the general assembly. Detailed rules will be formulated separately. (Article 7) After the organization is完善, it will be submitted to the superior party, government, and military agencies for record. (Article 8) If there are any omissions in these brief regulations, they may be amended by the meeting. (October 22nd)

Settlement of the Case of the Japanese Steamer Causing Trouble in Hankou 65

Japanese Side Admits Liability and Compensates for Losses

Hankou Correspondence: On the evening of the 18th, the steamer of the Japanese warship Hirado, which was docked in Hankou, overturned a private boat belonging to Wang Chugan, which was docked at the Sixth Wharf. The goods in the boat and the cargo escorts all fell into the water. The Japanese Vice-Consul visited Ye Peng, the Chief of Staff of the Garrison Headquarters, on the evening of the incident, requesting mediation and settlement to avoid escalating the negotiations. Ye believed that this matter was related to local security, but because he did not know the truth, he could not handle it rashly. He agreed to investigate first and ordered Jin Jutang, the Chief of the Staff Office, and Ren Benzhao, the Chief of the Investigation Office, to be responsible for the investigation. If it only involved local security and did not reach the level of formal negotiations, it could be handled accordingly to avoid escalation. Jin and Ren, the two Chiefs, went to the scene of the incident late at night to investigate the situation of the boat collision and questioned the boatman and cargo escort. According to the cargo escort, there were a total of three people escorting the cargo on the boat, plus the boatman, a total of four people. After the boat was overturned, only three people were rescued. The remaining one person, surnamed Gao, named Heshang, was not rescued. As for the sunken goods, there were more than 20 bags of soybeans, one bag of "爪子" (unknown product), plus the sunken boat, totaling about 300 yuan in losses. According to the boatman, another boat was also salvaging when the steamer was rescuing people. It was unknown whether Gao Heshang had been rescued. Jin and Ren, the two Chiefs, asked what Gao Heshang's occupation was. It was said that he was a waiter at the Ning-Shao Wharf. They then dispatched two investigators to the Ning-Shao Wharf to inquire. Before long, the dispatched investigators found Gao Heshang. Jin and others believed that since the person had been completely rescued, the case would be easier to resolve. They reported the investigation situation to Chief of Staff Ye. After Ye gave instructions, he still ordered them to negotiate with the Japanese Consul. After Jin and Ren received the order, they negotiated with the Japanese Consul and the captain of the Hirado face to face. The Japanese captain shirked responsibility and hoped to avoid compensation. After Jin and others refuted him, he had no excuses. Seeing that the Japanese side had yielded, Jin then proposed a method of compensating for the losses. In the end, it was agreed to compensate for the losses with 300 yuan, and the victims agreed to close the case. Jin also verbally warned the Japanese side that in the future, steamers must be more careful when sailing on the river to avoid similar incidents from happening again. On the 19th, the Japanese Vice-Consul went to the police station again and personally handed over the 300 yuan for compensation, which was transferred to the victims for collection and the case was closed. (October 23rd)

168th Meeting of the Legislative Yuan 66

The Legislative Yuan held its 168th meeting at 8:00 AM on the 24th. Thirty-five members, including Shi Shangkuan, were present. Shao Yuanchong presided over the meeting. The following matters were discussed: (1) The draft regulations on the Central Industrial Testing Institute of the Ministry of Industry were revised. It was resolved to submit it to the Legislative Committee for review. (2) The draft regulations on the screening of incumbent civil servants from military organizations and literature and art schools were reviewed and formulated. It was resolved to submit it to the Legislative Committee in conjunction with the Military Affairs Committee for review. (3) The draft amendment to the organizational regulations of the Central Health Testing Institute was revised. It was resolved to submit it to the Legislative Committee for review. (4) The Drafting Committee of the Autonomous Law of this Yuan reported and explained the regulations for the exercise of governance rights. For the fourth item, the amendment to Article 34 of the County Organization Law and Article 11 of the Civil Servants Disciplinary Law, how should the procedures for disciplining and dismissing commissioned district chiefs and civil servants below the recommended level be applied? It was resolved to pass the review report.

7th Division Holds Autumn Maneuvers 67

Xuzhou Correspondence: Wang Jun, the Commander of the 7th Division, has scheduled the autumn review for the current period and will hold autumn maneuvers in eastern Xuzhou from the 23rd to the 26th of this month. The troops of the 7th Division are stationed in the eastern and western sections of the Longhai Railway and the Bengbu area of the Jinpu Railway. Except for those stationed in Bengbu who could not be transferred in time, the troops stationed in Xuzhou were drawn up into two mixed brigades to conduct field confrontations, divided into east and west armies. The east army was composed of Wang Kaizhen's troops from the 37th Regiment and the troops directly under the division headquarters. The west army was composed of Gao Qikun's troops from the 38th Regiment and Du Run's troops from the 40th Regiment. Wang personally served as the chief judge, with Deputy Division Commander Li Shiding serving as the chief judge of the east army and Chief of Staff Zhang Jiankui serving as the chief judge of the west army. Qiu Yude, the Chief of the Staff Office, and Zhou Tirenn the Education Director of the cadre team, served as the judges of the east and west armies, respectively. The troops departed by car on the 22nd under the supervision of Li Shilong, the commander of the 19th Brigade, and concentrated separately. Wang Jun led the judges in a special train east this morning (the 23rd) to conduct the review himself. The east army departed from Guanhu Town, and the west army departed from Daxujia, confronting each other along the Longhai Railway. A considerable encounter battle can be made near Bayiji. Some personnel from the 7th Division accompanied Wang. It is expected to be completed in four days and then gathered for comments. (23rd)

Local Correspondence

Suzhou 68

The water patrol team in disguise captures the bandit leader. Cheng Delong, the captain of the water patrol squadron stationed in Guangfu Township, learned that Liu Zhengfu, the bandit leader in the Zhang Xushan kidnapping case in Xishan West Village, was hiding in Guangfu Town and demanding 20,000 yuan from Zhang's family. Therefore, on the 23rd, he secretly sent Patrol Captain Cai in disguise to go to the address and arrest Liu Zhengfu, who confessed to contacting twice but denied being the bandit leader. A farmer's family in Zhouzhuang Township was robbed. At about 9:00 PM on the 23rd, more than a dozen bandits suddenly came to the home of farmer Lü Fulai in Xidu Township South Village, Zhouzhuang Township, Suzhou, and carried out a search and robbery, resulting in heavy losses. A farmer's boat parked at the door was also robbed by the bandits.

The Department of Finance sent personnel to thoroughly investigate the license tax dispute. The oil, wine, sauce, candle, and tobacco industries in Suzhou jointly accused Chen Henian, the Director of the Wu Kunjiang Tai Tobacco and Wine License Tax Bureau, of illegally collecting excessive amounts and engaging in deception and corruption. They requested a thorough investigation from the Suzhou Department of Finance and the Ministry of Finance to maintain commercial operations. The Department of Finance specially sent Inspector Zhu Fujun to Suzhou yesterday (the 24th) to investigate. After arriving in Suzhou, Zhu visited Shi Yunqing, the Chairman of the Chamber of Commerce, and inquired in detail about the situation. He also investigated everything with the Tax Bureau to report and review.

Qingpu 69

Presenting a petition to the county to transfer the mu donation to repair the weirs and ponds. Qingpu citizens Zhang Jijai, Pan Qijun, Hu Kaixian, Guo Zhaotang, Chen Kecheng, Lu Changmao, etc., telegraphed Chairman Ye of the Zhenjiang Provincial Government on the 23rd, saying, "The flood in Qingyi is extremely severe, the weirs and ponds are destroyed, and there is no money to repair and rehabilitate. I found that your government had previously ordered the transfer of unnecessary construction costs to disaster relief. I admire your concern for the people's suffering. It is proposed to ask your government to order the county to transfer the county road mu donation stored over the years to the cost of repairing the weirs and ponds in order to maintain agriculture and benefit the people."

Wuxi 70

The private slaughter of plowing cattle resulted in death. Jin Wanxing Slaughterhouse outside the East Gate of this county, near the railway under Miaogang Bridge, was in charge of slaughtering cattle. Because the transportation and slaughter of cattle were prohibited, the slaughterhouse did not dare to slaughter them openly during the day. At more than 6:00 PM the day before yesterday, a group of Mao Da slaughtered a cow. Because of the secret slaughter, the procedures were inevitably improper, and the owner was hit in the chest by the cow's horn, resulting in serious injuries and death. The owner, because of the private slaughter of plowing cattle, had violated the prohibition and committed a murder. He was greatly frightened and thought of a way to create a false impression, falsely claiming that he died from electric shock. He bribed the family of the deceased to hastily put the body in a coffin and did not report it to the Procuratorate of the County Court for an autopsy.

The silk factory has fallen into despair. Of the more than 40 silk factories in this county, due to the decline in the silk market and inability to maintain operations, only six-tenths are currently operating. Now the sales market is even more stagnant. Each dan of silk loses more than 400 taels. The silk factories have fallen into an unrecoverable situation. Most factories have prepared to temporarily suspend work in order to preserve their strength. After the Taifu Silk Factory went bankrupt and dissolved, the financial sector was greatly shaken. Those who temporarily suspended work include Yulun Dafeng Yisheng Yifeng Changyi Housheng and other factories. The rest are also preparing to suspend work. Tens of thousands of employees are in a state of panic.

Changzhou 71

The Provincial Party Department resolves the issue of traitors in Wujin. After the case of traitors in Wujin destroying the Party Department newspaper office and the anti-Japanese association occurred, the Provincial Party Department sent people to thoroughly investigate. The County Party Department and other groups reported by telegram. In the face of national crisis, all compatriots are indignant and unanimously opposed to Japan. Now, Guo Junfu and Hu Ruilin, inferior merchants in Wujin, dared to destroy the national salvation movement, gather crowds to destroy the Party Department newspaper office and the anti-Japanese national salvation groups, and beat Party affairs workers. It is extremely absurd and reactionary. Li Zonggang, the Director of the Public Security Bureau of the county, as the person in charge of the security of the county, did not know how to prevent this atrocity beforehand and came back to protect it afterwards. If he is not severely punished, how can law and order be maintained? The following methods were specifically proposed by the Executive Committee for resolution: (1) The Provincial Government should be informed to order the County Government to arrest the instigators Guo Junfu, Yu Yiqin, Hu Ruilin, Zhu Yuanpei, and all the murderers within a time limit and bring them to justice. (2) The Chamber of Commerce should be seriously warned. The Chairman, Guo Junfu, should be removed from his position. The Ge Qiu Silk and Cloth Industry Association should be dissolved. Hu Ruilin's shops, which have been sealed, should not be opened before the legal issues are resolved. (3) The Provincial Government should be informed to remove and severely punish Li Zonggang, the Director of the Public Security Bureau of the county. (4) The anti-Japanese association should be responsible together with the Chamber of Commerce for sealing up all the Japanese goods originally stored in the shops. (5) The two comrades Wu Wenbi and Lu Zao, who were beaten, should be properly treated by the County Party Department and await legal resolution. Articles 1, 2, and 3 of the above resolutions have been submitted to the Provincial Government for investigation and handling yesterday.

Jiangyin 72

The County Executive Committee pays attention to the Hua Cheng Japanese yarn case. The Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association held its first standing committee meeting on the 22nd to discuss the Chamber of Commerce's letter and inquiry about the Kaiping coal mine's plan to change its management and transport the coal from Japan to Cheng in order to maintain industry. It was resolved that the Chamber of Commerce should be informed that during this tense period of anti-Japanese activity, it would be inconvenient to load coal on Japanese ships for shipment to Cheng to avoid misunderstandings. The period for displaying enemy goods in each store should be extended to the 28th and all should be sealed up. The Chamber of Commerce should be notified to order the merchants to comply. If this is not done after the deadline, they will be confiscated once discovered. The request from the silk and cloth industry to withdraw the order to seal up enemy goods was not approved. In addition, regarding the Hua Cheng Japanese yarn, it is widely rumored that someone is secretly contacting a sale for 4,000 yuan. During this week's Premier Memorial Week, Wang Bingchu, an executive committee member from one district, reported that he had summoned the parties involved, Chen Zhongda, Wang Bingchu, Tang Kesheng, Zhu Fei, and Chen Hongmo, for talks yesterday afternoon, with Ren Hongxin speaking separately.

Zhenjiang 73

Chongming and Qidong should continue to be separated. Chongming and Qidong were originally one county. After the revolutionary army settled in the southeast, they began to be separated. It has been five years since then. Recently, Wang Qingmu and others from Chongming submitted petitions to the Provincial Government and various departments requesting that they be merged due to the various problems caused by the separation of Chongming and Qidong. The 439th meeting of the Provincial Government Committee was handed over to the three departments of Civil Affairs, Construction, and Finance for review. The Finance Department convened a meeting. It was heard that the result of the review was that the crux of this case was that 70 to 80 percent of the industrial owners in Qidong were from Chongming. On the surface, Qidong people bear too much burden, but in fact, it is all the pain of Chongming people. Moreover, the land price before the separation was 30 to 40 yuan per mu, but now it is less than 10 yuan, while the taxes are now heavier than before, more than doubled. It is really unbearable for Chongming people to ignore this for a long time. This is the painful reason why Chongming people repeatedly seek merger. However, in this time of internal and external troubles, the people's hearts are fluctuating. If there are sudden changes in the two counties, there may be inappropriateness. Therefore, it is advocated to continue the separation and first seek to resolve these difficult problems. It is proposed to ask the Provincial Government to dispatch capable officials to the two counties to find out the suffering of the people in order to seek relief. In the future, the two county magistrates will be convened to discuss and resolve the matter.

Yangzhou 74

Organizing a national goods cooperative. Since the incident in the eastern province, Wang Shaoping, Fang Shoumin, Zhang Zizhong, Lu Yangwu, Feng Baozhi, and others in the county have stated that it is difficult to maintain economic severance with Japan through repeated tragic incidents. Therefore, they organized a national goods consumer cooperative for the people to promote national goods in order to achieve the goal of permanently resisting Japanese goods. County Magistrate Chen Nanxuan and Zhang Chengzhong from the Yangzhou Cooperative Guidance Institute of the Provincial Department of Agriculture and Mines have joined the initiation and are actively carrying out the work.

Hangzhou 75

The child robbery and murder case is adjudicated. Eight-year-old Zi Baoxing, a farmer in Sandun Township, Hangxian County, was studying in a nearby elementary school when he was called back to school by Jiang Wenqing, the sixteen-year-old son of a neighbor surnamed Jiang. On the way, he snatched his earrings and ran away. Zi chased and shouted, and accidentally fell into a pond and drowned. When his family came, it was too late to save him. Jiang Wenqing was arrested and brought to the Hangzhou Local Court for examination and asked. The teacher proved that Wenqing did call him. The interrogator believed that there was a premeditation and prosecuted him for murder. The case has been concluded. The sentence was pronounced at 3:00 PM on the 24th. Jiang Wenqing was sentenced to twelve years of fixed-term imprisonment for premeditated murder.

High Yitai found a large number of Japanese goods. Continued notes. A large number of Japanese goods were found in the warehouse of High Yitai Cloth Shop in Yangbatou, Hangzhou, by the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association in coordination with the volunteer army of the工學院 (Engineering College). The manager, Fang Kunliang, and four others, including the accountant, were sent to the Anti-Japanese Association for temporary detention. It is now learned that the inspection of the store was completed after two days and nights. After the Japanese goods were brought to the meeting for review, more than 100 pieces were found to be Japanese goods with trademark certificates. The rest are still under review. It is reported that the store is too large, with more than 20 money houses, cloth shops, and various stores. Personnel have now been dispatched to conduct thorough inspections to severely punish the store.

Bengbu 76

A fire at the New New World. The New New World Theater on Huachang Street is a well-known entertainment venue here. The theater uses electric lights for evening performances. However, because it owed too much electricity bill, it was cut off by the Yaohuai Electric Light Factory. The theater had no choice but to ask someone to negotiate with the Electric Light Factory to supply electricity on the one hand, and temporarily switch to Tongchang Car Company's kerosene lanterns as a temporary remedy on the other hand. At 6:20 PM last night (the 22nd), before the performance started, a gasoline lamp on the upstairs backstage exploded because the worker pumped too much air into it. The fire broke out suddenly and spread to the curtains, causing a prairie fire. The fire brigade of the Public Security Bureau, the fire brigade of the transferred union, and the commercial fire brigade arrived one after another after hearing the alarm and put out the fire separately. However, because the fire took advantage of the wind, it spread to the thatched houses of the poor in the nearby Tiedao Lane and burned until after 8:00 PM, demolishing all the thatched houses nearby. The fire gradually died down, and the New New World, which had been in operation for many years, was completely destroyed. After the incident, an investigation revealed that the New New World had burned down 24 buildings and 77 thatched houses in the vicinity, affecting 59 households, with losses of about 20,000 yuan.

Letters

Letter from All Workers of Changxing Coal Mine 77

Recently, I read an article in your newspaper's Hangzhou Correspondence column, which stated that Changxing Coal Mine Bureau was robbed by bandits and the Director was killed. It mentioned that the cause of the incident was that the Director was usually very harsh to the workers and would reprimand and dismiss them for slight dissatisfaction, which caused the workers to harbor deep resentment. After investigation, since Director Zhu came to the mine three years ago, he has been promoted from Chief Engineer to Director. He has always treated the miners well and has been gentle and kind. Yesterday he was suddenly killed, and all the employees of the mine were almost unable to cry. I think your newspaper's rumors are untrue, and I dare to ask you to correct them to comfort the public. Sincerely submitted by all the workers of Changxing Coal Mine Bureau, October 23rd.

Education News Highlights

Jiangsu Education College Compiles and Prints a Small Series of 20 Books on Japanese Studies 78

Wuxi Jiangsu Provincial Education College is a place in the country specializing in cultivating talents for mass education and agricultural education. With more than 300 teachers and students, it has always been known for its unremitting efforts in exploring the theory of the two educations and studying the methods of implementation. Various experiments and extension projects have been carried out with remarkable results. Recently, in view of the progress of the anti-Japanese national salvation work, its fundamental method lies in awakening the masses and knowing the enemy and ourselves. Twenty kinds of small books on Japanese studies have been specially compiled and printed, covering all aspects of Japanese domestic politics, economy, history, geography, population, national character, diplomacy, military equipment, as well as the methods and current situation of invading our country's northeast, and the truth of this incident. Everything is collected without omission, and the writing is simple, especially its characteristics. It has now been completely published, totaling 100,000 words. The entire set only charges 50 cents for printing costs, with no commercial nature at all. Those who purchase the entire set will also receive a copy of "Japan's Active Policy towards Manchuria and Mongolia," a colloquial (translated) memorial presented by Tanaka Giichi to the Japanese Emperor. In addition, the college has also compiled and printed three types of anti-Japanese national salvation textbooks for mass schools, high, middle, and elementary, each only charging 3 cents for printing costs.

Returned Students from Japan Held a General Meeting Yesterday 79

Resolved to Request the Ministry of Education to Postpone Registration

Ministry of Education Counselor Zhu Did Not Accept

The delegation of the Chinese Students Association in Japan, and the Returned Students Association in Japan, held a general meeting at the Ping'an Hostel yesterday morning at nine o'clock. More than sixty people attended to discuss various important matters and resolved as follows: (1) Registration Issue: The Ministry of Education had issued a notice to returned students requiring them to register with the Municipal Education Bureau. In principle, this could be complied with, but the Students' Association had not yet received orders from the General Association in Japan, and the registration of returned students with the Students' Association was not yet complete. Therefore, the Education Bureau was requested to postpone registration. (2) Livelihood Issue: The Ministry of Education must provide a practical solution to the accommodation problem of returned students. Because before the work of resisting Japan and saving the nation is resolved, all students are willing to sacrifice their studies and engage in the anti-Japanese movement. After registration, the Ministry of Education should not disperse students to various schools, so as to carry out the task of resisting Japan and saving the nation. (3) If the Ministry of Education can allow the above two articles, the Students' Association will immediately start general registration. At 2:00 PM, the Association sent representatives Zhao Pingzhang and five others to the Municipal Education Bureau to meet Counselor Zhu, a representative sent by the Ministry of Education, and Inspector Lin, to request the implementation of the two items resolved by the Association. However, Counselor Zhu did not accept them, so the registration issue is temporarily difficult to proceed and must be resolved after the general meeting.
