East China Miserably Defeated in the Last Five Minutes 90

| Lost to Norsenburg Two to Three |

| A Scene from Group A Football Match |

The East China Football Team played its second game since its debut yesterday, maintaining a balanced situation with the British Army Norsenburg Football Team for 85 minutes. Unfortunately, they were defeated by the enemy in the last five minutes, resulting in a score of three to two. The 8,000 spectators in the baseball field all expressed regret. This was a scene from the Group A League.

East China Team Lineup Yesterday 91

Chen Jiaqiu Chen Yutian

Li Ning Li Yichen

Zhou Xianyan Tu Kaiyuan Dai Linjing

Guan Xunan Chen Hongguang

Chen Pu Xi Qiaosheng

Norsenburg Army Lineup 92

Elpo Hailsheng

Qixihuo Xeteer

Luo Lan Bao Man Favek

Luoshimei Madison

Bao En Yang Ge

East China Takes Defense as Offense 93

In the overall situation, the British army adopted a full-fledged aggressive doctrine. The activities of the five forwards were exceptionally vigorous, which was surprising, and they were worthy of being a heroic team that once shocked the world, but their shooting was inaccurate and their efforts were poor. East China held on tightly with two lines of defense. Li Ning's rescue and Zhou Xianyan's breakthrough made the British army helpless and almost created a draw. Seeing that the situation was fierce, East China adopted a strict defense policy. Norsenburg arbitrarily moved forward, leaving the interior empty. East China took advantage of this weakness, "got the ball, and flew forward at full speed." Therefore, although the ball was mostly in the East China position, coupled with the frequent mistakes of Norsenburg's two defenders, dangerous situations were seen on both sides from time to time. East China's rapid advance by taking advantage of opportunities was mostly due to the lack of distance and stability of Xi Qiaosheng on the right wing. Once they reached the goal, they could not attack, and although there were many opportunities, they were wasted. However, the team's performance should be considered top-notch.

Norsenburg Lost Color 94

Fox, an excellent British referee, blew the whistle to start the game. Norsenburg got the priority of kicking off. Tu Kaiyuan intercepted the long shot, and the five forwards flew forward as soon as they saw the ball. Li Yichen lifted a foot, a few inches away, and the second fly-in, Chen Yutian was a little slow, and failed again. The momentum of East China on the field made the British army lose color. Then, they attacked one after another. Yang Ge and Madison came side by side, triumphantly. Li Ning watched the changes calmly and sent the ball directly to the front. Five horses galloping in succession. Luoshimei missed a step, Chen Yutian took the opportunity to attack fiercely, and the ball flew diagonally away. Dai's center forward kicked the door of Norsenburg, and 8,000 people cheered like thunder. The British army did not expect such a magical army.

Came and Went at Will 95

One reversal and one return, unexpected. Less than two minutes after East China broke the door, Norsenburg also broke the door. Zhou Xianyan saw that the situation was not small, jumped out to defend it, and Norsenburg center forward Wilick could not wait to kick it in, forming a tie of one to one. Norsenburg continued to attack, and the dozens of yards of territory in front of the East China gate were all the activity area of the Norsenburg army. Chen Pu once sent a long shot, but Li Yichen did not hit it. Li Ning did it again, and the forwards rushed to the door. Dai Linjing attacked with his head, and Bao Man imitated, waving his brain and hitting it backwards. Loshilan saved a corner kick, the Norsenburg army was in danger, and East China entered a better state.

The First Half Was Indistinguishable 96

Tu Kaiyuan sent the ball thousands of miles, reaching the right corner. Chen Hongguang and Xi Qiaosheng advanced, Qixihuo went to save, and another corner kick was formed. Xi Qiaosheng was fortunate not to fail. Chen Hongguang broke into the chaos, and the East China team once again took the lead. Coming and going at will, the Norsenburg army came to attack again. Elpo circled and came, Chen Hongguang failed to stop it, and the ball had flown to the center forward. Falek quickly passed to the left wing Hailsheng, without relaxing, he immediately attacked. Zhou Xianyan picked it up and dropped it lightly. Accidentally, Madison had already rushed up and kicked it in. The first half ended without a win or loss.

Miserably Defeated in the Last Five Minutes 97

In the second half, the Norsenburg army attacked fiercely, and Zhou Xianyan almost became the target of arrows. The atmosphere suddenly became tense. Although the viewers praised Zhou's stability and non-loss, they also saw anxiety. Each time the British army attacked, Luo Lan rushed out and dragged it away. Chen Yutian shot sharply on the left as if to enter the door, but he was happy in vain. One attack and one defense, one advance and one retreat, holding each other down. Although Norsenburg's attack was fierce, the result was nothing. The situation had become a draw, and the change came unexpectedly. In the last five minutes, the Norsenburg army was surrounding and forcing East China to arrange a strict defense in front of the door, waiting for the ball to come. Zhou Xianyan's vision was obscured, and Xeteer shot through the gap and entered. East China was defeated by three to two.

De Phu Won the Grass Tennis Singles Final 98

| Three to One Victory over Qiu Feihai |

Qiu Feihai's Amazing Performance 99

| Efforts Strived and Failed |

Canadian famous tennis player Mr. De Phu has not been in China for long, but his reputation has risen. He is tall and erect, with arms over his knees. His serves are rapid and powerful, and his volleying is impeccable. The only drawback is that he is prone to wild fires. Once the wild fire breaks out, it will be overturned. In this grass tennis singles competition, he defeated strong opponents. Yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM, he played the final with our country's famous general Qiu Feihai at the French Chamber of Commerce. Mr. Qiu once defeated De Phu with three to two in the Rotary Cup competition. His skills are superb and his will is firm. The two are equally matched and are a pair of strong enemies. De Phu's victory in the first set and Qiu's defeat were expected. In the second set, Mr. Qiu's iron arm waved, and De Phu could not control it. In the third set, Mr. Qiu's efforts failed, and De Phu came from behind. In the fourth set, life and death were at stake. De Phu advanced fiercely, and Mr. Qiu's strength was exhausted. As a result, De Phu won three to one and won the championship. At the end, Mrs. McShell gave the award, shook hands with each other and dispersed.

| The Number of Wins and Losses Was Expected Early On | 100

Mr. Qiu lost nine out of ten in the first set. The truth in this is difficult to understand. Some say it is Mr. Qiu's accumulated habits, and others say that Mr. Qiu is familiar after being estranged. The reason seems insufficient, but the fact is indeed the case. Therefore, the general audience knew the fate of the first set early on and predicted that De Phu would win and Mr. Qiu would lose. As expected, they were all correct. However, Mr. Qiu was not in a situation of inevitable defeat. When it was four to five, a little effort might have reversed the situation. At the beginning, Mr. Qiu won the first two games, which greatly aroused the audience's excitement. De Phu dealt with it with all his strength, first forming two to two, and then adding three consecutive games, forming an advantage of five to two. Mr. Qiu drew from left and right, repeatedly hitting the enemy's key points, recovering two games, and hope arose suddenly. At four to five, De Phu won three consecutive games, and Mr. Qiu's energy declined. De Phu won the second set with six to four.

| Iron Arm Waves, Dominated the World | 101

The second set was Mr. Qiu's golden age and Mr. Qiu's masterpiece. The iron arm waved, dominated the world, lured the enemy close to the net, and then split it diagonally, causing it to not be able to return. Suddenly soft and suddenly hard, or left or right, causing De Phu's wild fire to break out, and he could not recover from a defeat. Mr. Qiu won the first three games, and De Phu saw him win back one game. Mr. Qiu used his means to control the enemy's life, and won two more games. From then on, the foundation of victory was laid. Although De Phu wanted to resist, it was difficult. As a result, Mr. Qiu won six to two.

| Life and Death Were at Stake, Efforts Failed | 102

The third set was a matter of life and death. Mr. Qiu's sharp energy was extremely strong. He was good at using strategies. De Phu's rapid serves and his skill in holding the net were not enough to deal with. He was invaded and lagged behind by three to five. It was a pity that Mr. Qiu was repeatedly tricked by the enemy, and his efforts failed. The overall situation was reversed, and De Phu took the upper hand again, and won the third set by seven to five. The two rested for a while and started the fourth set. De Phu knew his weaknesses, suppressed the wild fire, and acted cautiously. After each one, De Phu completed three games in one breath, with stern words and expressions. Seeing the overall situation, Mr. Qiu was in great danger, so he stood up and fought against the enemy. He won two consecutive games, his spirit came, and hope was born. At this time, the score was Mr. Qiu three and De Phu four. Unexpectedly, Mr. Qiu's strength was exhausted, and he lost one game by a net four, resulting in three to five, and then lost his hand with a net four. As a result, De Phu won the fourth set by six to three.

Diplomacy Emergency First Unity Against Foreigners 114

Guangdong Representatives are Negotiating in Shanghai

Cai Yuanpei Comes to Shanghai to Invite Them to Beijing for Discussion

Shao Lizi Speaks Optimistically About the Prospects of Peace Talks

Diplomatic Issues are Telegraphed at Any Time 115

According to a telegram from Nanjing yesterday, Cai Yuanpei and Zhang Ji arrived in Beijing the day before yesterday and met with Chairman Jiang and various committees of the Central Government. They immediately telegraphed the Guangdong representatives in Shanghai, Wang Jingwei and others, saying that diplomacy is important. I hope you will come to Beijing immediately to discuss it together. Then, they received a reply telegram from Wang Sun and others, saying that the colleagues do not ignore the importance of diplomacy at all. If there is anything to be seen, they will telegraph it at any time. After receiving the telegram, Cai Zhang immediately informed Chairman Jiang and various committees of the Central Government. Cai Zhang also came in person to urge them to come. Regarding all matters, I hope that the representatives of Guangdong will come to Beijing to discuss them in person, so as to avoid the waste of letters and messengers. Also, the Nanjing Special Diplomatic Committee telegraphed Shanghai on the 23rd to Yu Youren to be forwarded to the Guangdong representatives, reporting the seven mediation methods proposed by the League of Nations. I hope that you will come as soon as possible so that you can decide how to deal with them. However, there was no reply telegram as of the afternoon of the 24th.

A Diplomatic Committee Will Be Established First 116

The Peace and Unification Conference has not been held yet because the representatives from Nanjing have not yet been determined, so there is no definite date for the preparatory meeting. The Guangdong representatives Wang Jingwei and others, because of the urgency of diplomacy, intend to establish a diplomatic committee before the Peace Conference to deal with the urgent needs. It is also heard that Chen Youren, Wu Chaoshu, and other important diplomatic talents will be responsible for it when it is established in the future, but this layer also depends on the opinions of Nanjing.

Words and Actions of the Guangdong Representatives Yesterday 117

Yesterday morning, the Guangdong representatives held their usual morning talks at Wang's residence on Seymour Road. At 10 o'clock, Wang Jingwei, Sun Ke, Chen Youren and the three others went to Hu's residence on Meyer Road for talks. They left near noon and returned to their respective residences for lunch. Wang did not go out in the afternoon. Sun went to Wang's residence in the afternoon and returned at 3 o'clock. Wu Chaoshu, because Mr. Bai Yunti had arrived in Shanghai, was eager to meet with Mr. Zou Haibin, so at 3:00 PM, he had arranged to meet with Zou at Wu's residence and had dinner at Wu's residence. In the afternoon, more than a dozen people visited Hu's residence one after another, including Zhang Fakui, Lian Shenghai, Miao Bin, Chen Jintao, and Guo Taiqi. It is said that most of what they talked about was diplomatic issues.

Shao Lizhi Discusses Peace Talks Optimistically 118

Shao Lizhi Answers Questions from a Guest: (1) I came to Shanghai based on personal relationships. Although I enjoyed meeting with representatives from the Guangdong faction, I did not participate in any meetings concerning the planning of the party and the nation. However, I am certain that both sides are earnest and sincere. When discussing important issues, progress is smooth. Because both domestic and foreign troubles are pressing, no comrade of our party should allow personal opinions to cause suspicion and disagreement. Only mutual concession and trust can save the critical situation. (2) Regarding the future improvement of the party's and government's policies, in addition to Cai Yuanpei, Zhang Ji, and Chen Mingshu, the Central representatives will also include Li Shizeng and Zhang Renjie to discuss matters with the Guangdong representatives. (3) I am not yet clear about the establishment of a unified foreign affairs committee. The date for the Guangdong representatives to come to Nanjing has not yet been determined. (4) Is Chairman Chiang going to Shanghai again? It seems unnecessary to go again at this moment. All issues will be discussed by representatives from both sides, and Chiang will follow the majority opinion. The rumors that Chiang will return immediately after going, and that peace will not proceed smoothly, are not true.

Cai Yuanpei Returned to Shanghai Yesterday 119

Central Committee members Cai Yuanpei and Zhang Ji recently went to Nanjing to report on the progress of the peace talks in Shanghai. Mr. Cai returned to Shanghai at 8 a.m. yesterday, while Zhang remains in Nanjing. After getting off the train, Cai returned to his private residence for a short rest, then visited Wu Tiecheng, Chen Mingshu, Zhang Jingjiang, and others for meetings. He also visited Sun Ke at the Sun residence on Rue Molière, and then returned to his private residence on Route Say Zoong Field to rest. In the afternoon, those who visited Cai's residence were not received.

Chen Mingshu Went to Nanjing Yesterday 120

After meeting with Cai Yuanpei yesterday, Chen Mingshu believed that there were important matters that needed to be discussed with Chairman Chiang in person. He took the Nanjing-Shanghai express train to Nanjing at 3:15 p.m. yesterday.

Anti-Japanese National Salvation Movement 123

The Anti-Japanese Association held an executive committee meeting yesterday; the Hou Dachun case was sent to the party headquarters for handling.

The Shanghai Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association held its tenth executive committee meeting yesterday. More than 40 committee members attended. Fu Dewei was publicly elected as chairman, and Zhao Shusheng and Tong Yikang served as recorders. The following matters were reported: (1) The measures for disposing of confiscated Japanese goods have been drafted and were approved and amended by the twelfth standing committee meeting and reported to this association. (2) The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce's announcement on the implementation of the economic severance committee has been published in the newspaper for implementation. The announcement was approved by the eleventh standing committee meeting and reported to this association. The following cases were then discussed: (1) The case of Committee Member Hou Dachun being accused was reviewed by the review committee, and a resolution was requested. It was resolved that: (A) In accordance with the review report, the case will be transferred to the municipal party headquarters for handling. (B) Before this case is resolved, Committee Members Feng and Hou should continue to recuse themselves. (C) Hou Dachun should be required to return the 500 yuan of relief funds from this association that he damaged. (D) Chen Ji, the current director-general of the investigation department (i.e., the former director-general of the inspection section), should be dismissed. (E) The review report and resolution should be published in various newspapers. (F) The documents related to this case should be sealed by the review committee and handed over to the chairman for safekeeping. (2) The rules for punishing traitors drafted by this association should be reviewed. It was resolved to appoint Wang Pingnan, Li Cishan, and Yu Hualong as review committee members, with Wang Pingnan designated to convene the committee. (3) The measures for rewarding and punishing those who secretly report Japanese goods have been drafted and should be approved. It was resolved to appoint Xie Fusheng, Ren Jinping, and Chen Yafu as review committee members, with Xie Fusheng designated to convene the committee. (4) Should the request of Committee Member Yan E to resign from the position of director of the secretariat be approved? (5) The case of Committee Member Zhao Shusheng requesting to resign from the position of deputy director of the secretariat. (6) The letter from Mr. Wu Kaixian requesting to resign from the disciplinary committee. It was resolved to combine the discussion and retain them. (7) Three proposals compiled by Committee Member Zhang Zilian based on the suggestions of the Shanghai Copper, Iron, and Machinery Industry Association should be discussed. It was resolved to hand them over to the standing committee. (8) Should the application of Lao Yongchang Coal Company to guarantee Ding Fangyuan, an employee of Bao Da Xiang Foreign Cloth Store, be approved? A resolution was requested. It was resolved to approve the release on bail, with the requirement to appear whenever summoned. (9) Should this association send letters to Taikoo and Jardine Matheson Companies, requesting that they not lease Nissin Kisen Kaisha's ships? A resolution was requested. It was resolved to pass the resolution.

Measures for Disposing of Confiscated Japanese Goods 124

Passed by the Standing Committee of the Anti-Japanese Association

The Shanghai Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association's measures for disposing of confiscated Japanese goods have been approved by the twelfth standing committee meeting of the association. The original text is as follows: (1) All confiscated Japanese goods should be used entirely for disaster relief and should be notified to the disaster relief committees of various provinces to promptly provide relief in the disaster areas. (2) For confiscated Japanese goods that are large and cannot be used for disaster relief, this association should entrust the municipal chamber of commerce to contact overseas Chinese merchants in Southeast Asia and India, transport these Japanese goods to those ports, sell them cheaply to non-Chinese residents, and allocate the proceeds to disaster relief funds. (3) For confiscated Japanese goods that are small and scattered, a public announcement should be published in the newspaper, and they should be burned on a selected date. (4) The first and second measures should be completed by this association as soon as possible, so that the victims can receive practical benefits as soon as possible.

The Business Community Should Take an Oath to Economically Sever Ties with Japan Immediately 125

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Informs Various Trade Associations to Comply

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to various trade associations and commercial organizations yesterday, stating: "Regarding the case on the 22nd of this month, according to a letter from the Shanghai Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association, it was found that the seventh executive committee meeting of this association discussed the suggestions of the design committee to send a letter to your association to notify various trade associations, and to send letters to various institutions, organizations, and schools that have not yet taken the oath, should take an oath to obey the scope and measures of the economic severance of ties with Japan as stipulated by this association during the Sun Yat-sen Memorial Week on Monday. This case was approved and recorded. It is hereby recorded and notified, and we hope that your association will check and implement it."

The Municipal Federation Implements Inspection of Japanese Goods 126

Organize a Japanese Goods Inspection Committee

Inspectors are Equipped with Badges

In order to implement the economic severance of ties with Japan, the Shanghai Municipal Citizens' Federation, after a resolution at a general meeting, organized a Japanese Goods Inspection Committee, which dispatched inspectors uniformly the day before yesterday. The details are recorded as follows:

Implementing Inspection 127

The Citizens' Federation organized a Japanese Goods Inspection Committee. The committee members are Wang Zhaocheng, Liu Zhongying, Wang Jingdong, Xu Yunhui, Lin Yangzhi, Ye Qichang, Wu Ban'an, Jin Yuqing, Zhang Heng hai, Jiang Xianhe, Shi Jiulin, etc. Each district branch may organize a Japanese Goods Inspection Group, with each group consisting of five to nine people, and they have already been established one after another. Inspections will be dispatched from the 21st of this month. If Japanese goods are found in any business, they will be sealed up immediately and reported to the municipal federation at the same time. The municipal federation will send personnel to re-examine. All inspectors wear badges. After the inspection, each business fills out a letter of determination, stating: "From today onwards, I voluntarily swear not to buy or sell Japanese goods. If I violate this vow, I will accept public punishment. This matter concerns national salvation, and I hereby make this vow to show my determination."

Inspection Regulations 128

Regulations of the Japanese Goods Inspection Committee of the Citizens' Federation: (1) This committee may at any time lead the inspection committee members of each branch to carry out their work in any store within the special zone that has Japanese goods. (2) Each district branch may establish an inspection committee, with a number of people ranging from five to nine. (3) This committee will meet twice a week to discuss matters related to the inspection of Japanese goods. (4) This committee will supervise the inspection matters of the branch committees at any time and create a register for reference. (5) If the inspection committee members of the branch committees encounter difficulties in their work, they should report to the municipal committee for handling. (6) If any inspector of this district and the branch committees encounters insults or other circumstances while on duty, the citizens' association of the special zone should do its best to protect them, regardless of any sacrifice. (7) All inspectors in the Ping District and branch committees are on a voluntary basis and do not receive any allowance. (8) If any inspector of this district and the branch committees engages in extortion, blackmail, or other illegal acts while working outside, they will be punished according to law. (9) The methods of this committee are from 9:00 a.m. to 4:00 p.m. (10) These regulations will be implemented immediately after they are passed.

Various Guangdong Circles Organize an Anti-Japanese Association 129

The various circles of Guangdong in this city, deeply angered by the brutality of Japanese imperialists, especially the Japanese thugs who often provoke incidents and insults in the North Sichuan Road area, have joined together to organize the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association, including the Guangzhao Public School, the Shanghai branch of the Lianyi Society, the Xinhui Township Association, the Shanghai Gold and Silverware Industry Association, and other 30 organizations, and issued a declaration to express their patriotic enthusiasm.

Overseas Chinese Purchase Airplanes to Resist Japan 130

Truly Noble Deeds of Practical National Salvation are Commendable

Donating Ten Thousand Yuan to Purchase Airplanes for War Preparation

According to Mr. Xu Shengli, a leader of overseas Chinese in Penang, who is currently in Shanghai, since the terrible news of the Japanese forcibly occupying the Northeast and massacring compatriots spread, the overseas Chinese in Penang have felt deeply indignant. In addition to vigorously advocating anti-Japanese national salvation work and implementing economic severance with the brutal Japanese, they also requested the National Government through the Penang Reading Society, voluntarily donating funds to purchase fighter planes for use in the future war with Japan, and first remitted a donation of 10,000 yuan through the Hefeng Bank, entrusting Mr. Xu Shengli, the chairman of the society, to personally hand it over to the Nanjing National Government. The Penang Reading Society was personally organized by Sun Yat-sen when he lived overseas in Penang, British Malaya, and the Tongmenghui was attached to it. Although the society is called the Reading Society, it is actually the overseas headquarters of the revolution. At the beginning of the Xinhai Uprising, revolutionary leaders from various overseas ports convened a meeting at the society to jointly plan the overthrow of the Qing Dynasty and the restoration of the Han Dynasty. Later, during the anti-Yuan campaign and the May Thirtieth Movement, members of the society spared no effort to take the lead in promoting their enthusiasm for protecting their motherland, which is a true example for the overseas Chinese community. This grand move of donating funds to purchase airplanes has been highly praised by the National Government and the public. It is reported that Mr. Xu Shengli is scheduled to enter Nanjing within the next few days to discuss everything with the National Government authorities. It is expected that the overseas Chinese in various ports will be very enthusiastic when they hear the news.

The National Salvation Women's Volunteer Army Held a General Membership Meeting Yesterday 131

Resolved to Form an Executive Committee to Carry Out Association Affairs

Military Training Will be Conducted After the General Meeting is Established

Since the Japanese army invaded our Northeast, women's circles in this city have risen up to take actions to save the country. Tang Baiyu, Shao Xiangling, He Jinzhi, and three others from the women's academic circles initiated the organization of a women's volunteer army as a support for anti-Japanese national salvation. Those who have joined are quite enthusiastic. Yesterday, a general meeting was held at the county party headquarters, with more than 100 people attending. It was named the Shanghai Women's National Salvation Volunteer Army, and seven executive committee members were elected to hold an inaugural meeting on a scheduled date to conduct training. Details are recorded as follows:

Meeting Details 132

After the meeting proceeded as planned, Chairman Tang Baiyu first reported on the purpose of the meeting, stating briefly that at this critical moment of national survival, male compatriots have already awakened and organized a volunteer army to strengthen national defense capabilities, and our women's circles should also be armed in unity, hence the initiation of the women's army. Then, He Dinghua, a representative of the Women's Relief Association, and Jiang Yanqiu, a representative of the county party headquarters, gave successive instructions, followed by speeches from guests from various circles. Representatives were then elected to discuss the proposals.

Approved Proposals 133

(1) Passed the constitution of the army. Resolved to amend and pass it. (2) Stipulated the training time and location. Resolved to hold training every Saturday from 2:00 p.m. to 3:30 p.m. and every Sunday from 8:00 a.m. to 9:00 a.m. (3) Stipulated the style of clothing. Resolved to imitate the men's army uniform, with dark blue color. (4) Elected executive committee members. Resolved that in addition to Shao Xiangling, He Jinzhi, and Tang Baiyu as ex officio executive committee members, Zheng Manzhen, Zhou Liyah, Duanmu Yan, and Zhu Zhixian were publicly elected as formal executive committee members. (5) Send a telegram to the whole country to unite and conclude an alliance for anti-Japanese national salvation. Resolved to pass it. (6) Publish a notice in the newspaper to inform women from all walks of life to strive to participate in the army, engage in military training, and increase national strength. Resolved to pass it.

Passed Constitution 134

Article 1: This army is named the Shanghai National Salvation Women's Volunteer Army. Article 2: The purpose of this army is to unite patriotic women, engage in military training, strengthen national armed forces, and vow to resist Japan and save the country. Article 3: Any female citizen of the Republic of China who is over 16 years old, physically strong, and has a definite spirit of sacrifice for the country may become a comrade of this army. Article 4: This army will be established and start training as soon as 30 people are recruited, and will continue to recruit comrades and expand the establishment at any time. Article 5: This army will elect five to seven executive committee members and three alternate executive committee members from the general meeting to form an executive committee to handle all affairs of the army and training matters. The initiators are ex officio executive committee members. Article 6: The uniforms of the comrades of this army will be purchased by each person, and the style, material, and color will be decided by the general meeting. Article 7: The expenses of this army will be borne by all comrades in principle, tentatively set at 20 cents per person. Article 8: The executive committee members and military instructors of this army are all voluntary positions. Article 9: The general meeting of this army will be held once a month, and the responsibility for convening it will be borne by the executive committee members. The executive committee will meet once a week. If one-third or more of all comrades request it, and it is approved by the executive committee, a temporary general meeting may be convened. Article 10: The detailed rules for the executive committee's handling of affairs will be formulated by the executive committee. Article 11: The address of the executive committee of this association is temporarily borrowed from Zijin Primary School. Article 12: If there are any matters not covered in this constitution, they may be amended by the general meeting. Article 13: This constitution will be implemented after it is passed by the general meeting.

Zhang Yaozeng's Letter of Admonition to the People (Continued) 136

Am I truly not one of these who, holding the responsibility of leading politics, lacks the spirit of public service, acts like a master at home and a slave abroad, makes exclusion the main task, seeks old grievances to take revenge, only seeks to be dictatorial, and does not hesitate to let the whole country fall into paralysis? Called leadership, but only to allow individuals to amass power, empty words are like a raging fire, but in reality, nothing is accomplished? This is the root cause of chaos and weakness. Am I truly not one of these who, in a difficult situation, harbors resentment against the world and seeks a living through destruction, incites class struggle, and overturns social order? This is the root cause of chaos and weakness. Am I truly not one of these who does not engage in production and relies on others for survival, revolves around the people, and runs between generals? Alliances are formed and broken, plans are made, and right and wrong are based on self-interest, treating national affairs like a game of chess? This is the root cause of chaos and weakness. Am I truly not one of these who, holding a public office in the state, only

Page 14

thinks about hoping for glory and solidifying his position, perfunctorily dealing with everything, and not seeking results, or indulging in literary elegance and considering inaction as the highest virtue, or gambling and indulging in debauchery, abandoning his duties? This is the root cause of chaos and weakness. Am I truly not one of these who engages in business without following the right path, or colludes with the government to obtain illegal wealth, or deceives the public and greedily seeks unjust profits, or takes advantage of danger to obtain by trickery, or divides profits and sits idly by? This is the root cause of chaos and weakness. Am I truly not one of these who does not seek truth, but flaunts his ability to view lecturing as a method of planting party members, does not diligently study and practice, but seeks to expand his influence, and regards entering school as a shortcut to participating in politics? The academic atmosphere is becoming increasingly superficial, and academic achievements are becoming increasingly scarce? This is the root cause of chaos and weakness. Am I truly not one of these who is dedicated to his profession, accumulates assets, preserves his life, supports his wife and children, and lives peacefully and keeps to himself, but ignores the chaos and does not feel responsible for national affairs? This is the root cause of chaos and weakness. Am I truly not one of these? Consider each of these things, and if I have even one of them, then I am the root cause of chaos and weakness. The coming of foreign insults is truly my fault, and there is no need to blame other compatriots. If I have even one of them, then I am the root cause of chaos and weakness. The responsibility for correcting the chaos and strengthening the country lies with me, and there is no need to blame other compatriots every day. Everyone thoroughly understands their sins, and everyone thoroughly corrects their mistakes, and then everyone can truly forgive each other, truly love and care for each other, and then the whole country will have extraordinary unity and extraordinary strength. Only then can we talk about the method of resisting the brutal Japanese. The method of resisting the brutal Japanese can be decided in one word: national mobilization. Total mobilization does not mean that everyone goes to the front line. It means that everyone should do their best in their duties with the heart of going to the front line. All my compatriots who have military talent and experience, whether new or old, party members or non-party members, in or out of office, are not allowed to refuse or evade. They should rise up together and quickly form a complete national defense from the sea, land, and air. They should have strict discipline and meticulous planning to prevent changes, control opportunities, kill enemies, and achieve results. All my compatriots who have political talent and experience, except for those who do not have national or nationalistic ideas, regardless of new or old, party members or non-party members, in or out of office, should rise up together and strive for national defense, either by jointly organizing a national defense government, or by separately implementing local autonomy, or by guiding national public opinion, or by enriching national movements, each choosing their abilities and performing their duties with utmost sincerity, to use diplomacy, to warn and inspire the people, to maintain order, to pacify the local areas, to stabilize finance, to promote production, and to prepare military supplies and armaments, so that the front has nothing lacking and the rear has nothing to worry about. All my compatriots who are engaged in production and support themselves, regardless of agriculture, industry, commerce, or other occupations, in addition to resisting Japanese goods and materials, should also strive to investigate and study diligently to find substitutes for raw materials that have always been supplied by foreign countries in our own country, and to invent and produce methods for products that have always been unable to be manufactured in our own country, and to make the technology that has always been indispensable for perfection capable of being perfected by our own people. All parties should work together to create a self-sufficient and independent economy with no dependence in the shortest possible period, and at the same time restrain waste and redouble their efforts. Luxury and unnecessary needs should be avoided. While other countries work eight hours, we should work twelve hours, so that production will increase day by day and national strength will increase day by day. (To be continued)

Review Report on the Hou Dachun Case 137

Regarding the Hou Dachun case, the Anti-Japanese Association organized a review committee to review it. This review report was also resolved and published by the tenth executive committee meeting of the association. The original text is recorded as follows: "The committee members have convened meetings twice, on October 22nd and 24th, according to the instructions of the general meeting to review the case of Hou Dachun's report and Feng Yixian's accusation that he embezzled public funds. Hou Dachun, Feng Yixian, and relevant persons Wang Yongliang and Chen Ji were also invited to the venue. After examining various evidences, the results of the review were resolved as follows: (1) The temporary record book of the inspection section before July 24th (recorded by Chen Ji, director-general of the inspection section) shows that Director Hou received 500 yuan. According to Chen Ji, he knew at the time that this amount was donated by the Commercial Press. At that time, only 400 yuan was handed over by Director Hou himself, and the remaining 100 yuan was paid for the expenses of the Zhabei district. I (Chen Ji) made a note of it. I am willing to take responsibility for this point." (2) Hou Dachun's letter to the Commercial Press on July 23rd, and the payment list of the Commercial Press, and even the final reply from the Commercial Press stating that they received the amount, all specify that this 500 yuan is a fund for assisting refugees. (3) The donations for the refugee relief fund, as well as the registration income and fine income, were all collected and remitted by the members of the economic committee, and collected by the banks and money houses designated by the general meeting. However, the receipts of the banks and money houses for collecting the relief fund, and the dispatch book of the Refugee Relief Association, stated that they were sent out only on August 1st. On July 24th, the banks and money houses were not yet responsible for collecting the funds. (4) On July 24th, the use of funds by the Refugee Relief Association was not yet settled. Hou Dachun, because he was responsible for inspection, temporarily misappropriated the donations he received. (5) The funds received by the inspection section were never sufficient, and there was never a fact that more than 500 yuan of cash was accumulated. The staff in the section almost did not consider repaying the amount. (6) After the reorganization of the inspection section into the investigation department, the previous accounts should be settled, but at that time, the remaining funds in the section were only 262 yuan, 2 jiao, 3 fen, and 5 li. On September 28th, a receipt was signed, totaling 237 yuan, 7 jiao, 6 fen, and 5 li, and received from the accounting office. By August 4th, the amount of 500 yuan received from the accounting office was completely collected. According to proper procedures, the amount should be returned to the place where it should be received. However, Chen Ji, the director-general, still kept the amount with himself, claiming that it was because the investigation department had a plan to organize a special team and would keep it for misappropriation. (7) On the morning of October 20th, Hou Dachun took the deposit of 500 yuan from Chen Ji and returned it to the Commercial Press, and retrieved the receipt for the relief fund issued in Hou Dachun's name. Based on the above facts, the following conclusions can be drawn: (1) The refugee relief fund donated by the Commercial Press was used as office expenses for the inspection section without a resolution from the general meeting or the standing committee, nor was it reported to the general meeting or the standing committee. It was freely disposed of, which was not without the suspicion of acting beyond authority, and invited criticism. (2) The account book uses the name of Director Hou to receive the account, which clearly shows that the amount belongs to Director Hou. The record is indeed inappropriate, but who should bear the responsibility is still a matter for study. (3) The 500 yuan of refugee relief fund donated by the Commercial Press was no longer related from the time it was donated, and was transferred to the entire anti-Japanese refugee relief association. No one should dispose of it without authorization. Hou Dachun returned the amount directly to the Commercial Press, which is questionable in terms of law and reason. (4) Hou Dachun received the amount directly, and after Wang Yongliang took it, he handed it over to the inspection section. Until the time of return on October 20th, he had never put the amount into his own hands, and it seemed that he had no intention of embezzling the amount. (5) Feng Yixian is a member of this association and serves as the secretary. He did not report the case to the executive committee or the standing committee, nor did he report the situation of his report to the central government to the executive committee. He published it to the outside world as much as possible, which seemed to disregard the reputation of this association. The review opinions are as follows. How to deal with it is requested for public decision. Review Committee Members Wang Pingnan, Chu Huiseng, Li Cishan, Xie Fusheng, Chen Yafu. October 24, 1931.

Case of Japanese Thugs Shooting Chinese Police 138

Japanese Consul Speaks Ambiguously

The City Government Requests a Reinvestigation

Regarding the case on the 21st of this month at 12:15 AM, in which Japanese national Nishimura, Matsumoto, and Taiwanese Huang Kuanju, among others, riding in a car on Route Doumer and East Yokohama Road, intentionally provoked City Public Safety Bureau police officer Wang Changgen and shot him, the City Government conducted a detailed investigation that evening. The next morning at 9:00 AM, a verbal protest was lodged with the Japanese Consulate, followed by a formal written protest that afternoon, making three demands: (1) Strictly punish the troublemaking Japanese nationals Nishimura and Matsumoto; (2) Swiftly restrain the Japanese residents to prevent further incidents that increase Chinese resentment; and (3) Reserve the right to further negotiations. After the protest note was delivered, the Deputy Consul Mr. Shirai from the Japanese Consulate gave a verbal reply to the City Government the day before yesterday afternoon. A reporter from the New Voice News Agency visited Mayor Zhang yesterday to inquire about this matter. Mayor Zhang received the reporter, but since Secretary-General Yu had received Deputy Consul Shirai's response that day, Secretary-General Yu provided the reporter with a detailed account of the negotiations. He stated that Mr. Shirai's response was that the Japanese Consulate had investigated and learned that Nishimura and Matsumoto had not carried guns that day and, having been drinking, would have been unable to carry them. Therefore, the reason for the shooting of the Chinese police officer was that the officer attempted to fire his gun, and the Japanese national, struggling with him, accidentally triggered the weapon. He requested that the City Government reinvestigate. Furthermore, he claimed that when the bullet pierced the Chinese police officer's wrist, the Japanese national was also injured. His statements were contradictory. I immediately refuted this, saying that the City Government had conducted its own investigation in segments since 12:30 AM that day, completing it by 8:00 AM this morning. The factual details were extremely clear. If Nishimura and Matsumoto had not carried a handgun, how could the D'Autreuil Road precinct have found a cartridge casing from a Browning pistol afterward? The Chinese police officer carried a Mauser, so it could not possibly have been fired by him. As for saying that they would not have carried guns after drinking, that is simply absurd. If the Japanese Consulate had investigated clearly, why did it say both that the two sides were struggling and accidentally triggered the gun and that the Chinese police officer fired the gun himself, piercing his wrist and injuring the Japanese national? In law, the facts must be absolutely consistent, and there is no room for ambiguity. After this refutation, the Deputy Consul was left speechless and again requested a reinvestigation and fulfillment of the protest conditions.

City Chamber of Commerce Requests Ban on Increased National Coal Freight Rates 140

Yesterday, the City Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Ministry of Railways regarding the increased freight rates for national coal on the Jiaoji Railway, requesting a swift ban. The telegram stated: "To the Ministry of Railways in Nanjing, according to a telegram from the Shanghai Coal Industry Association, 'The Japanese aggression is universally condemned. Economic severance with Japan is the citizen's duty and a unanimous demand. Japanese coal is no exception. Southern provinces have historically consumed two-thirds of the total amount of Japanese coal. Now that sales are refused, national coal must be transported to replace it. If the transport of national coal is delayed, the southern provinces will face a coal shortage. If there is a shortage, warships, merchant ships, trains, and all factories, lights, and waterworks will cease functioning. This situation is extremely dangerous. As of October 20, Shanghai has only 300,000 tons of coal, enough for only one month. It is urgent to transport national coal to replenish the supply. However, the Jiaoji Railway's Traffic Director, a Japanese national, is seizing this opportunity to increase national coal freight rates, effective November 1. The special export rate of 2.52 yuan per ton is now increased to 2.8 yuan. Shandong mines are reportedly halting operations. This behavior is tantamount to harming our national life. Besides urgently telegraphing the central government to order a halt, we request assistance to cancel the Jiaoji Railway's coal freight increase to avoid a coal shortage, as it concerns the nation's fate. Please grant assistance.' Therefore, as economic severance with Japan is strictly enforced, national coal should be promoted. Now, it is claimed that the Jiaoji Railway's Traffic Director, due to his Japanese ties, is seizing this opportunity to increase national coal freight rates, causing Shandong coal mines to halt operations. If this is true, the impact on coal use in central and southern provinces is significant. We hereby telegraph this information to your office, requesting a swift order to stop this, in the public interest. Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce bows."

Overview of Yangtze River Shipping 141

Observations on the Rise and Fall of Three Nations' Steamers

Chinese Steamers Arrive in Shanghai One After Another 142

Since May 17 of this year, the Transportation Department of the General Headquarters has chartered a total of 20 Chinese merchant steamers on the Yangtze River routes in Shanghai, lasting for half a year. Now, various steamship companies, such as China Merchants, Sanpei, Ning-Shao, and other Yangtze River passenger lines, require ships. Therefore, the General Headquarters has been requested to release the chartered ships. Approval has been granted, and the Jiangshun, Jiang'an, Jianguo, Jiangxin, Fengpu, and Xin Ningxing, among others, are returning to Shanghai from Nanjing. Chinese ships have been operating on the Yangtze River since the 21st. The General Headquarters has retained a few Jiangyu, Jiangtian, and sea-going vessels. The rest will be released continuously. Therefore, from November 1, full operations can resume, restoring the original state of Yangtze River steamers before the war.

All Ports Can Now Load Cargo 143

During the major floods on the Yangtze River, the lighters and warehouses in Wuhu, Anqing, Jiujiang, and Datong were submerged. At that time, the Six Companies in Shanghai notified all passengers that storage of lighter cargo was suspended and that loading was refused in Shanghai. Now that the floodwaters have receded, the situation has long been restored. The Six Companies can now load as much cargo as possible in Shanghai bound for Nanjing, Wuhu, Anhui, Xunyang, and Hankou, without restriction.

British Ships' Business is Congested 144

In the past two months, Tai-Koo and Jardine on the Yangtze River have dominated the business. (1) The floodwaters in Wuhan and other places have receded, and goods and construction materials are being loaded upstream in Shanghai. (2) Chinese steamships have not resumed operations. (3) Chinese merchants everywhere refuse to transport Japanese ships. Due to these three reasons, Tai-Koo and Jardine's export business in these two months has been unprecedented in decades. Each ship can collect over 10,000 taels in freight from Shanghai's cargo alone. On average, in the past two months, Tai-Koo and Jardine have earned at least 1.5 million taels on the Yangtze River route. Therefore, these two companies are now very serious about loading cargo and refuse to make any concessions, requiring full payment. Jardine used to send four ships per week, but now they are dispatching one ship per day.

Japanese Ships Fail to Be Chartered 145

This newspaper reported earlier about the leasing of Japanese ships to a certain British trading firm in Shanghai. Now, the Qing Company's Shanghai steamers are unable to operate because the Captain has resigned, and all services have been suspended. The company has eleven ships on the Yangtze River route. For the past two months, there have been no cargo or passengers. The company intended to lease them to the British, but due to popular opposition, fearing damage to their business, the British firm firmly refused. Recently, the company also received a notice from our national shipping association and dared not lease the ships. It is now heard that the Japanese merchants can only grit their teeth and resume services, fearing that the ship licenses will be revoked if they stop operations. Currently, the company is losing at least 130,000 to 140,000 yuan per month on the Yangtze River route.

Yangtze River Freight Rates Increase 146

During the major floods on the Yangtze River, the Six Companies increased freight rates to Anqing, Jiujiang, and Hankou by 10% to cover flood expenses. Now that the floodwaters have completely receded, it was agreed yesterday to abolish these flood expenses from November 1. However, at the same time, it was agreed that from November 1, export cargo from Shanghai to Zhenjiang, Nanjing, Wuhu, Datong, Anqing, Jiujiang, and Hankou will be subject to a 15% increase over the original prices.

National Goods Alliance Holds Second Committee Meeting Yesterday 147

Organizing Inspection Teams to Depart for Inspections

The National Goods Promotion Alliance Committee held its Third Second Committee Meeting yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM. Ye Jinkang, Ma Jisheng, Wang Hanqiang, Ji Jiannan, Zhang Qingfa, Xu Genghua, Sun Daosheng, Wang Xingyi, Yang Yucheng, Chen Yiyan, Chen Xin, Lu Zhuang, Xiang Songmao, and others attended. (4) Review the measures drafted by the inspection team and publish them in the newspaper immediately to notify national goods factories. (5) Reply to the Cosmetics Industry Association based on the resolution. (6) Convene the Design Committee on Monday. The measures decided by the inspection team are excerpted as follows: 1. Divide into five inspection teams, each with one committee member and one staff member. 2. Collect factory listings from the four groups, categorized by industry. 3. When departing for inspections, invite one or two experts from each industry to identify goods. 4. Prepare a form to notify each factory, setting a deadline for reporting Japanese raw materials.

7,000 Tons to Arrive in Shanghai on December 3

A draft plan for its use and distribution has also been prepared and will be discussed at the regular meeting on the 28th. The distribution plan is recorded as follows: (1) Total amount for emergency relief is 93,000 tons: 9,300 tons in October, 18,600 tons in November, 23,250 tons in December, 18,600 tons in January of year 21, 18,600 tons in February, and 4,650 tons in March. (2) Total amount for agricultural relief is 50,000 tons: 15,000 tons for seed loans in October and November, including 1,400 tons for Jiangsu, 4,000 tons for Anhui, 4,000 tons for Jiangxi, and 5,600 tons for Zhejiang and Hubei, and 15,000 tons for lending to civil engineering projects in December, and 20,000 tons for lending to civil engineering projects in January, but (1) American wheat cannot be used as seed, and suitable seeds for local land should be exchanged at market prices with merchants during lending, (2) The grain lent out should be returned to the agricultural relief fund for the purpose of restoring agriculture, and (3) Total amount for work relief is 300,000 tons: (Explanation) Each disaster worker is given wages based on their work performance, averaging 15 catties of wheat per day. Each American ton has 1,500 catties, and each month has 30 days. Each American ton is enough to pay 10 disaster workers for one month's wages. Recruit 35,000 new people in November, using 3,500 tons of grain. Recruit another 70,000 people in December, totaling 105,000 people, using 10,500 tons of grain. Recruit another 100,000 people in January of year 21, totaling 205,000 people, using 20,500 tons of grain. Recruit another 150,000 people in February, totaling 355,000 people, using 35,500 tons of grain. Recruit another 200,000 people in March, totaling 555,000 people, using 55,500 tons of grain. Recruit another 100,000 people in April, totaling 655,000 people, using 65,500 tons of grain. Stop recruiting workers from May onwards and disband 150,000 people, using 58,000 tons of grain. Disband another 400,000 people in June, using 30,500 tons of grain. Disband another 75,000 people in July, using 6,750 tons of grain. Disband another 20,000 people in August, using 2,000 tons of grain. Disband another 10,000 people in September, using 500 tons of grain. Reserve 11,250 tons. (The amount of grain used after May is estimated based on the average number of days in that month.)

Page 15

Local News 2

Bandits Shoot Down from Above, Three Detectives Seriously Wounded 151

Wu Tianbao Luckily Escapes the Law

Only His Wife and Concubines are Captured

All Three Detectives Severely Injured

Yesterday afternoon around 2:00 PM, a robbery and capture battle occurred on Route Pettit in the French Concession, leaving three detectives seriously wounded and in critical condition. The details are as follows:

Repeated Major Cases in Hangzhou 152

The notorious bandit Wu Tianbao, from Shaoxing, has repeatedly committed kidnapping and robbery in Hangzhou and elsewhere. After the case was reported, the County Public Security Bureau issued an arrest warrant. Last month, detectives from the Hangzhou County Public Security Bureau discovered that Wu was hiding in the attic on the third floor of 25 Shengping Lane on the Avenue Edward VII in the Shanghai French Concession. They immediately prepared a document and reported to the French Concession police, who dispatched detectives to assist in the arrest. Wu was out on business at the time, and only four suspects, Wang Yongfu, Zhang Yongxiang, Wu Yuntang, and Wu Dechang, were captured. Eleven bullets were seized and sent to the Second Special Court for questioning, but they were released after being found not related to the case.

Traced to Hiding in Shanghai 153

Although Wu escaped the law, the Hangzhou police authorities continued to exert all efforts in the investigation. The Hangzhou County Public Security Bureau learned that Wu was hiding on the second floor of 1 Beidifang on Route Pettit in the French Concession. Yesterday morning at 11:00 AM, the Bureau's Detective Chief Jiang Zhongyun (Zi Jinquan, 27 years old) and informants took the document directly to the French Concession police.

Bandits Shoot Down from Above 154

Around 1:00 PM, the police chief ordered detective Ni Jinrong of the 114th precinct (from Jiangbei, 35 years old), detective Zhao Chunsheng of the 174th precinct, and Zhao's partner Wang Jinyu (from Jiangbei, 27 years old) to assist Detective Chief Jiang in the ambush. When they arrived at Beidifang, they found the front door of number 1 tightly closed. Asking the gatekeeper, they were told that the front door had never been opened. The detectives then rushed through the back door from the adjacent alley. Unexpectedly, the bandits upstairs had been alerted. Wu pulled out a handgun, waiting in ambush at the top of the stairs, attacking from a high vantage point.

Opening Fire in the Face 155

As the detectives reached the middle of the stairs, the bandit opened fire, striking head-on. The bullets came like linked beads. The detectives could not dodge and also drew their guns to return fire, but aiming upwards proved difficult. As a result, Detective Zhao and the informant remained guarding outside the door, fortunately unharmed, but the rest, Jiang Zhongyun, Ni Jinrong, and Detective Partner Wang Jinyu, were all seriously injured. Because the bandit's marksmanship was accurate, most of them were hit in the head.

Three People Collapsed by the Stairway 156

Seeing that all the detectives were wounded and fallen, Wu took the opportunity to escape to the drying terrace and fled without a trace over the rooftops. By the time other detectives rushed in upon hearing the commotion, the three men were already lying in a heap by the stairway, bleeding profusely. Detective Zhao quickly took his gun upstairs, capturing Wu's wife, Wang (26 years old), and concubine, Yang (26 years old). He seized a loaded handgun and immediately telegraphed the police station, which dispatched a large number of detectives to surround and search, but to no avail.

Highly Secretive Movements 157

The three injured men were immediately taken by car to Renji Hospital for treatment. Jiang was shot in the throat, Ni in the temple and leg, and Zhao's partner Wang Jinyu had the most severe head injuries. All were feared to be in danger of death. The detectives searched everywhere again, but the house was empty. It was heard that Wu was a subtenant and the main tenant had fled, fearing involvement. Wu had been renting the house for more than four months. There was only his wife and concubine at home. Wu and his wife smoked upstairs all day, and no one had ever seen him at night. The daily chores were done by his concubine, but his wife went out every night in a rickshaw from the alleyway, and her movements were highly secretive.

Noulens Defends Himself 158

Excellent Treatment in Detention

Since being arrested in Shanghai last month and transferred to Nanjing for trial, international communist leader Noulens has had his Far Eastern redization plan and various subversive documents searched and translated by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs in conjunction with the Central Propaganda Department. Yesterday, rumors spread that Noulens had been sentenced to death, but this is not confirmed. Noulens is currently detained in Nanjing, provided with Western food and servants, and receives excellent treatment. He is currently being questioned, and his lawyer is defending him.

Rice Prices in the City are Falling 159

Recently, rice prices in the northern and southern markets of this city have been gradually falling due to the ample supply of new japonica rice from various places, exceeding demand. Yesterday, the highest price for premium white japonica rice in the northern market was 15 yuan per dan, and another was 14.6 yuan. Regular new japonica rice was 13.5 yuan per dan, and another was 13.3 yuan. Western new japonica rice was 14.2 yuan per dan, and another was 14 yuan, a drop of about half a yuan compared to the previous two days. Compared to the middle of last month, the difference is nearly three yuan per dan. According to people in the rice industry, although the low-lying areas in various villages suffered from continuous rain, causing disaster and submerging fields, the autumn harvest was diminished, but the low-lying areas are a minority. Some areas were submerged but later the water receded and the fields were restored. Others suffered partial damage from submersion, while only a few had no harvest at all. As for the highlands that were not affected by the flood, the autumn harvest was better than in previous years. In the Pudong villages near Shanghai, the net harvest was around 3.2 to 3.3 dan per mu. In the villages of Changshu and Wuxi that were not affected by the flood, the harvest was more than 3 dan per mu. Therefore, the overall production is quite abundant. Currently, farmers in various villages do not dare to hoard and are rushing to sell, so the market price is likely to continue to fall.

More Small Parks to be Opened in the Public Concession 160

The Municipal Council announced yesterday that the issue of increasing open spaces in the Public Concession continues to be closely monitored. Today, each district in the Concession needs to add parks, but in practice, this issue is best handled in cooperation with the municipal authorities in the city because land prices are high and there are many new buildings making it difficult to find larger open spaces for recreation purposes. If land is to be found outside the Concession, the permission and cooperation of the Shanghai Municipal Government is required. Since the opening of parks, the number of Chinese visitors has increased and the existing parks are not sufficient. There is an increasing demand for more, but there are no suitable gaps in the Concession. The only option is to add small parks outside the Concession, where land prices are cheaper, to provide recreational space for children. The Public Works Department Chief has suggested that the homes of every citizen should be within half a mile of a large park of 20 to 40 mu for children's recreation.

Red Cross Disaster Relief News 163

The details of the Wuhu Relief Team dispatched by the Shanghai Chinese Red Cross, carrying medicines and biscuits from the Times and Bazaar relief station, have been previously reported. We have now received a report from the team members Ji Heqin, Bao Kang, and Shen Jintao that after arriving in Wuhu on the 19th, they were welcomed at a meeting by various organizations. Since then, the disaster relief work has been quite busy. The disaster is most severe in the Shenshan area of the northern countryside. Along the way, passing Yuanze Bridge, Xianxinwei, Waiyang Village, Xiawuji, Hengtangpu, Zhujia Village, and Gaojiazhuang, the water has receded slightly, but the villages are in ruins. The flooded area spans tens of miles, a vast expanse of water. Mules, livestock, fields, and crops are all submerged. As far as the eye can see, there is no trace of human life. In the midst of the rising cold wind, the scene is particularly bleak. In Taishan, disaster victims are crowded together, waiting to be fed. The biscuits they brought will be distributed at half a pound per bag, with a ticket, and can be given to over 40,000 people, but there are still many people. It is like a drop in the ocean, of no help. The Gaochun biscuits released have been taken away by Director Wu Yushu, and 106 boxes must be sent to Dangtu. It is planned to be distributed personally, depending on the time and traffic.

News from the Suzhou Flood Relief Association 164

"Yangzhou is Actively Conducting Disaster Relief Efforts" The association recently received a telegram from its Yangzhou office, stating that the disaster relief process in Yangzhou begins with setting up shelters to accommodate and care for the displaced. Then, relief goods are distributed for emergency assistance. Subsequently, multiple porridge kitchens are established in key areas to provide regular meals for nearby victims. The distribution of wheat seeds and the maintenance of farm cattle are also being carried out in sequence. Personnel have been dispatched to Gaoyou, Baoying, Xinghua, Taixing, and Dongtai counties, as well as Tangtou, Fancha, and Shaobo towns, to transport large quantities of cotton clothing and bedding donated from Suzhou. The Jiangdu area is extensive and severely affected, and a survey of households is underway to plan winter relief efforts. These are the major relief measures. Additionally, small businesses inside and outside the city that have been slightly flooded have suffered unemployment rates of 80-90%. The original loan office, limited by insufficient funds, has now been supplemented with 1,000 yuan to expand the loan amount under the interest-free loan principle. The Gongdao Bridge in the ninth district was destroyed by the flood, and the villagers cannot afford to repair it. 2,500 yuan has been allocated for repairs to provide work-for-relief opportunities. The funds for the latter two items will be drawn from the Suzhou-raised relief funds.

Pacific Science Congress, Day Four 165

In the afternoon, delegates from various countries went to Hangzhou.

China's population suffers from density imbalance.

Exploiting natural resources can regulate it.

The Shen Shi Telegraph Agency reports that the Pacific International Science Congress held its fourth day of meetings yesterday. A round table meeting began at 9:10 a.m., continuing discussions on "China's Economic Development Issues." Due to the break on Saturday afternoon and the departure of committee members for Hangzhou, the content of the discussions could not be published. From 11:10 a.m. to 12:10 p.m., a summary was made of the opinions on China's economic development that had been discussed over the past few days. At 12:10 p.m., a joint meeting of the agenda committee and the chairman's secretary was held. At 12:30 p.m., the Chinese delegation hosted a banquet for all committee members. In the afternoon, delegates from various countries departed from the North Station to Hangzhou on a special express train on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway at 2:10 p.m. The translation of Mr. Rockhill's speech on "China's Population Problem" from the previous evening is as follows. Mr. Rockhill stated that the population problem of China is a riddle. Opinions vary, so statements also differ. Some estimate China's population at 450 million, while others believe it to be less than 300 million. It is thought that the Chinese government should have an accurate survey. It is probably no more than 400 million, accounting for a quarter of the world's population. This saying has been around for a long time, so foreigners once made a joke: "When people ask how many children a family has, if there are four, they always say three, because the fourth is Chinese." The problem is not overpopulation, but imbalanced density. According to Italian statistics from 1928, there are 348.9 people per square mile. In Denmark in 1925, there were 207 people per square mile. In France in 1926, there were 191 people per square mile. According to a recent survey in Japan, there were 407 people per square mile. In China, according to a 1929 survey, Jiangsu has 813.1 people per square mile, Hebei 583, Zhejiang 554, Anhui 389, Henan 376, Hubei 359, Jiangxi 283, Shanxi 164, etc. Mongolia averages only three people per square mile. The uneven distribution of population density is evident. Furthermore, China has not yet been able to utilize its natural resources. For example, the grasslands of Mongolia can accommodate 450,000 people, and mountain areas outside the plains can be used for animal husbandry, forestry, and planting. Adapting to local conditions and developing accordingly, wherever human economic conditions can be exploited, can solve the current problem of population regulation. At the same time, solving the population problem requires facilitating transportation, promoting education, revitalizing agriculture, and researching the utilization of natural resources in border and mountain areas, which are the most urgent tasks at present. In addition to the research and discussion of general scholars, it is ultimately said that China can simultaneously control fertility, improve the family system, and improve public security, which are crucial to solving China's population problem.

One Thousand and Seventy Yuan 169

Thieves only stole seventy yuan

Jin Guitao was shot and robbed

Jin Guitao, a 45-year-old man from Shaoxing, residing at No. xx, Changren Lane, Baoxing Road, Zhabei, is a fishmonger. Yesterday afternoon at 5:10 p.m., he was carrying paper money totaling 1,070 yuan, sealed in two packages, one for 1,000 yuan and one for only 70 yuan, to pay the bill at the Chen Deji fish shop on Caisheng Street in the French Concession. Not far from his destination, five or six thugs suddenly appeared, brandishing handguns, threatening and intimidating him. As a result, they only managed to snatch one paper package containing 70 yuan from his pocket. The thugs then fled with their loot. Guitao, upon seeing this, immediately followed behind, shouting for help to stop the robbers. This was seen by one of the thugs, who, fearing that the police would arrive upon hearing the shouts, fired a shot, hitting Jin in the thigh, causing him to bleed profusely. By the time the patrol arrived, the robbers had gone far away, and they could only transport the injured man to Renji Hospital for treatment.

Fire in Changan Road, Zhabei 170

Yesterday afternoon at 5:25 p.m., a barber shop named Changan Barber Shop, located at No. 381 Changan Road, Zhabei, run by Mao Quankun from Yangzhou, suddenly caught fire. In an instant, flames burst through the roof, and the fire spread rapidly, engulfing the neighboring Dakang Sheng Hotel at No. 385 and the storefronts at Nos. 379, 377, 375, and 373, including a hardware store, a sesame cake shop, and the overpass buildings at No. 387 Qiu'an Lane, destroying a total of seven shops and houses. The fire brigades from various districts rushed to the scene and worked hard to extinguish the fire. After about an hour, the fire gradually subsided. The owner of the barber shop fled the scene immediately. A tenant, Qiu Pengshi, was detained by the Japanese police officer of the Second Station of the Fourth District for questioning. It is said that they had only moved in a few days ago and that the fire started in the main room of the barber shop. When the fire broke out, the Second Station of the Fourth District was nearby, and they quickly moved the guns to another location. Chief He led the entire squad of police chiefs to the scene to maintain order. Later, it was discovered that the shop had fire insurance, raising suspicions of arson. It is reported that an old man from Qingjiang, Qiu Jungui, 61 years old (living in the kitchen of the shop, the husband of the detained Pengshi), had his beard and eyebrows burned off by the fire, but fortunately, he was rescued by the police, otherwise he would have been buried in the fire.

Pig Vendor Beaten and Falling into the River, Lawsuit Filed 171

Wu Rongbiao's injuries are not fatal

Wu Rongbiao and Wu Shunlong, two brothers from Jingjiang who sell pigs, came to Shanghai to trade at the Changyuan Pig Firm in Xuejiabang. The other day, Wu Shunlong was suddenly beaten by people from the pig firm on the boat due to a trivial matter and fell into the river, drowning. His body was nowhere to be found. Wu Rongbiao filed a complaint with the First Precinct of the First District, and Wu Jiyong, Shi Qingjiang, Zhang Sisan, and others from the Changyuan Pig Firm were arrested. Later, the body was recovered by the Lifesaving Bureau. They reported to the District Court to send someone to verify that although the deceased had injuries on his body, they were not fatal. It was verified that he had drowned after being injured and falling into the river. The family members were ordered to collect the body, and the defendants were transferred from the police station to the court for questioning yesterday.

Butcher's Wife-Killing Case Opens 172

Sentencing to be announced at a later date

Qin Shoufan (also known as A Si), a butcher from Haimen who worked as a pig slaughterer at No. 55 Yuezhou Road, took his wife, Zhang (32 years old), to his brother's house at No. 3248 Zhoujiazui Road at 11:30 a.m. on the 19th of this month. He accused her of having an affair and demanded the return of 30 yuan of travel expenses, but she refused. Angered by the argument, he stabbed her in the leg and abdomen with a sharp blade, killing her. The prosecutor of the First Special District Court went to Fielun Road for an autopsy. Qin was arrested by Chinese detective Yan Qingxi and Western detective McLoughlin of the Harbin Police Station. The details of his interrogation at the autopsy site have been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, Judge Shen Bingrong presided over the third criminal court to hear the case. Zhang Tianyin, the lawyer for the police station, stated the case and said that no other evidence had been found during the postponement. He then submitted the autopsy report and the sharp blade for investigation. When questioned, the defendant confessed that Zhang had come to Shanghai from his hometown on the 11th of this month, and on the 13th, he gave her 30 yuan to return home quickly. On the 18th, he received a letter from his father from his hometown saying that she had not returned home. He was very surprised and found out that she had an affair with a Fan at No. 50 Jiaxing Road. So, that morning, he secretly went to Fan's place and found her, but Fan was not at home. He then took her to his brother's house to reason with her. On the way, she said that her lover had already squandered the money and that if he wanted money, he could sell her for two yuan a time. When they arrived at his brother's house, he tried to search her for money, but she grabbed a sharp knife from the side and stabbed him. He disarmed her and, in a fit of rage, stabbed her three times in the leg, but only to scare her into repenting, not intentionally to kill her. At that time, he was confused and did not know where he was stabbing her. He then went outside and told his brother to send her to the hospital. Soon after, his nephew came and informed him that she had died. He intended to surrender to the police station but was arrested by Chinese and Western detectives on Zhaofeng Road. According to his brother, Qin Shoulian, the sharp knife submitted as evidence was indeed from his home. His sister-in-law, Zhu, testified that she was in the bedroom at the time and heard a noise. When she went out to look, Zhang had already been stabbed and fell to the ground. She did not know who had stabbed her first. Western detective McLoughlin stated that the deceased had knife wounds on both her left and right legs, which were stabbed by the tip of the knife, and the knife wound on her lower abdomen was quite severe, penetrating through. The wound on the back was larger. This was witnessed by another Western detective named Hunter, who told him. Judge Shen appointed a lawyer to defend the defendant and then ordered Qin Shoufan to be remanded in custody, pending sentencing at a later date.

Verdict in Fecal Carrier's Manslaughter Case 173

Sun Longyi sentenced to eight years imprisonment

Sun Longyi, a porter for a certain fecal company from Jiangbei, got into a dispute with his fellow villager Sun Ankui on a boat in the Shajing Road riverbank at 6:50 a.m. on the 16th of this month over carrying feces, kicking him in the abdomen, causing his death. Sun Longyi was arrested by Chinese detective Zhou Kaiwen of the Harbin Police Station and brought to the First Special Court. The deceased's wife, Sun Miao, hired a lawyer, stating that the deceased had an elderly mother and a two-year-old daughter to support, all relying on him alone. Therefore, she attached a civil lawsuit, requesting compensation of 5,200 yuan, etc. After the interrogation was completed, it was awaited for sentencing. Yesterday morning, Judge Shen Bingrong presided over the third criminal court, sentencing Sun Longyi to eight years imprisonment. The number of days detained before the final judgment was determined, with two days allowed to offset one day of imprisonment. The civil lawsuit portion was transferred to the civil court for trial.

Laborer Falls from Sixth Floor 174

Brain matter splattered, tragic death

Wang Xuecheng, a 39-year-old laborer from Funing at the Yutong Flour Mill on Guangfu Road, Zhabei, was operating a hoisting machine to lift goods to the sixth floor yesterday when he accidentally lost his footing and fell from a height, causing his brain matter to splatter and killing him instantly. Yong'an Textile Factory in Wusong Suspends Work Due to Machine Damage 175

Repaired on the same day

The Yong'an Second Textile Factory in the west of Yuncao Creek, Wusong, has been experiencing exceptionally prosperous business recently. The factory employs about 10,000 male and female workers. Therefore, during dismissal hours, the area is very crowded with male and female workers. Yesterday morning at 1:00 a.m., all the machines in the factory suddenly stopped. The workers who were working the night shift were released at 5:00 a.m. When the workers who were supposed to start work arrived at the factory gate, they all returned home. Upon investigation, it was discovered that the power supply pipe in the factory's main furnace room was damaged and could not be repaired, so all operations were temporarily suspended for a day. It was not until 5:00 p.m. that day that the repairs were completed. All the male and female workers entered the factory at 5:00 p.m. to start the night shift. It is said that the pipe is replaced every week due to the prosperous business and the heavy demand on the machines. Unexpectedly, it was damaged before it even completed a full week, which shows the quality of the factory's products.
